Three Legal Categories of Wudu: Fard, Wajib, and Mandub
Defines three legal categories of wudu and lists six disliked aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three legal categories of wudu (fard, wajib, mandub), identify the occasions for each, and list the six disliked aspects in the manner of performing wudu.

Core Idea
Wudu’s ruling varies: fard for prayer, wajib for tawaf, and mandub for sleep.

In this passage, the author explains that wudu does not always carry the same legal weight. It can be obligatory (fard), necessary (wajib), or recommended (mandub) depending on the action one intends to perform. Additionally, he highlights six undesirable practices to avoid while performing wudu, which help ensure the act is performed properly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three legal categories
From the passage, extract the three types: fard (obligatory), wajib (necessary), and mandub (recommended). Note the specific actions that trigger each category.
Fard is based on definitive evidence (qat'i), wajib on probable evidence (zanni).
2
List the occasions for each category
For fard: prayer (even nafl), funeral prayer, sajdat al-tilawah, and touching the Quran. For wajib: tawaf of the Ka'bah. For mandub: sleeping in a state of purity.
Omitting wajib requires dam (blood sacrifice) as compensation, while omitting fard invalidates the act.
3
Understand the six disliked aspects
From the beginning of the passage, note the six things that are makruh tanzihi: israf (extravagance), taqtir (stinginess), striking the face with water, speaking to people, seeking help without excuse, and repeating the wipe with new water.
Some of these may become haram in certain contexts, such as israf with waqf water.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a scenario (e.g., someone performs tawaf without wudu), determine the ruling and consequence using the categories.
Since wudu for tawaf is wajib, omitting it requires dam but does not invalidate tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أوصاف الوضوء ستة أشياء: الإسراف في الماء، والتقتير فيه وضرب الوجه به والتكلم بكلام الناس، والاستعانة بغيره من غير عذر، وتثليث المسح بماء جديد. فصل [في أوصاف الوضوء] الوضوء على ثلاثة أقسام: الأول : فرض على المحدث للصلاة ولو كانت نفلاً، وصلية ولصلاة الجنازة، وسجدة التلاوة، والمس القرآن ولو آية. والثاني: واجب للطواف وصلية بالكعبة. والثالث : مندوب للنوم على طهارة، وإذا استيقظ منه، أي القسم الثالث أي القسم الثاني فيجب الدم بتركه ويثبت بما يثبت به الواجب كما في "الفتح"، ومكروه تنزيهاً وهو ما تركه أولى من فعله، وكثيراً ما يطلقوته، فلابد من النظر في الدليل، فإن كان نهياً ظنّيّاً يحكم بكراهة التحريم ما لم يوجد صارف عنه إلى التنزيه، وإن لم يكن الدليل نهياً، بل كان مفيداً للترك الغير ،الجازم، فهي تنزيهية، قاله صاحب "البحر". حاشية الطحطاوي: ٨٠] ستة أشياء: ليس للحصر بل للتقريب للمبتدي. الإسراف : هو العمل فوق الحاجة الشرعية، في "فتاوى الحجة": یکره ره صب الماء في الوضوء زيادة على العدد المسنون والقدر المعهود، وفي "الدر": ويكره الإسراف فيه تحريماً لو بماء النهر أو المملوك له، أما الموقوف على من يتطهر به ومنه ماء المدارس - فحرام [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٨٠] والتقتير : أي بجعل الغسل مثل المسح فيه بأن يقرب الغسل إلى حد ،الدهن لكن لابد من أن يقطر ولو قطرتين حتى يكون غسلا، وإلا فلا يصح الوضوء أصلاً، والتقتير : هو عدم بلوغ الحد المسنون، فلو اقتصر على ما دون الثلاث قيل: يأثم، وقيل: لا، وقيل: يأثم بالاعتياد [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۸۱] ضرب ويرسل الماء على الوجه من أعلى الجبهة برفق، ثم يدلكه به. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۸۱] الوجه ومثله غيره من بقية الأعضاء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۸۱] بكلام الناس: أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن له حاجة تفوته بتركه، فإن كانت له حاجة وتفوته بترك التكلم في الوضوء فلا. ثلاثة: العدد لا يفيد الحصر، فلا ينافي أنه قد يكون مكروهاً، كالوضوء على الوضوء قبل تبدل المجلس الأول، أداؤه عبادة لا ت لا تصح بدونه به، وقد يكون حراما كما إذا كان من ماء الوقف والمدارس. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٨٢] فرض : المراد بالفرض هنا الثابت بالقطعي، فالمراد الوضوء من حيث هو بقطع النظر عن أجزائه، وأما المحدود والمقدار، فهو ما يفوت الجواز بفوته ليشمل الفرض الاجتهادي كربع الرأس. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٨٢] ولو آية مكتوبة على درهم أو حائط مراقي الفلاح على طهارة ظاهره أنه لا يأتي بذلك المندوب، إلا إذا أخذه النوم وهو متطهر ، فلو تطهر ثم اضطجع وأحدث فنام لا يكون آتيا به [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٨٣]
Descriptions of wudu: six things: extravagance in water, stinginess in it, striking the face with it, speaking with people, seeking help from others without excuse, and repeating the wipe with new water. Chapter on descriptions of wudu: Wudu is of three types: First: obligatory (fard) upon the one in a state of minor impurity for prayer, even if supererogatory, and for the funeral prayer, the prostration of recitation, and touching the Quran even if one verse. Second: obligatory (wajib) for tawaf of the Ka'bah. Third: recommended (mandub) for sleeping in a state of purity and upon awakening from it. (Commentary explains wajib requires blood sacrifice if omitted, and defines makruh tanzihi, etc.)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage opens the section on 'Descriptions of Wudu' (awsaf al-wudu) by first listing six disliked aspects in the manner of performing wudu: extravagance in water (israf), stinginess (taqtir), splashing water on the face, engaging in conversation with people, seeking assistance from others without excuse, and wiping the head with new water thrice (tathlith al-mash). The commentary clarifies that these are not exhaustive but approximations for beginners. It then divides wudu into three categories based on legal obligation: First, fard (obligatory) for anyone in minor impurity when intending to pray (even nafl), for funeral prayer, for sajdat al-tilawah, and for touching the Quran (even a single verse). Second, wajib (obligatory but not fard) for tawaf of the Ka'bah; leaving it requires a dam (blood sacrifice) as compensation. Third, mandub (recommended) for sleeping in a state of purity and upon awakening from sleep. The commentary elaborates that 'fard' here means that which is established by definitive evidence (qat'i), and includes ijtihad-based fard like washing a quarter of the head. The commentary also re-emphasizes the definition of makruh tanzihi (leaving it is better than doing) and reiterates that the six things are makruh tanzihi unless otherwise specified (e.g., israf from waqf water is haram). There is a note that the number three does not indicate exclusivity; other acts may also be makruh or even haram, like performing wudu with water from a waqf.

Key Terms
الإسراف (al-israf): Extravagance in water usage beyond the legally recommended amount (three washings per limb).
التقتير (al-taqtir): Using too little water such that the washing is nearly like wiping; at least two drops must drip for validity.
الفرض الاجتهادي (al-fard al-ijtihadi): An obligation established by ijtihad, like washing a quarter of the head (as opposed to the whole head according to some).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling for someone who performs tawaf without wudu?
A) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated
B) The tawaf is valid but a dam is required
C) The tawaf is valid without compensation
D) The tawaf is haram

Key Takeaway
Wudu is fard for prayer and Quranic touch, wajib for tawaf, and mandub for sleep; its performance requires avoiding six disliked acts to ensure completeness.

Conditions for Obligation of Prayer
States conditions for prayer obligation and categorizes fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the obligation of prayer and distinguish between fard ayn and fard kifayah.

Core Idea
Prayer is obligatory only on Muslims who are sane and have reached puberty.

The Book of Prayer begins by establishing who must pray. The author lists three conditions without which prayer is not obligatory. The commentary further clarifies the types of fard and the training of children, setting the foundation for the entire jurisprudence of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Read the first sentence: Islam, puberty, and sanity are required for prayer to be obligatory. Without any of these, the individual is not commanded to pray.
These are shurut al-wujub (conditions of obligation), not validity conditions.
2
Understand the obligation on children
The text orders commanding children to pray at age seven and beating (lightly) at ten for neglect. This is training, not obligation—the conditions are not yet fulfilled.
The beating is done only with the hand, not a stick.
3
Distinguish fard ayn and fard kifayah
The commentary explains that prayer is fard ayn (individual obligation), which every accountable Muslim must perform, unlike fard kifayah (communal obligation) like funeral prayer.
Fard ayn cannot be dropped by others' performance.
4
Note the result of missing a condition
If any condition is absent (e.g., a child, non-Muslim, insane), prayer is not obligatory. However, once attained, the person must make up missed prayers? This is a separate issue.
The text does not discuss qada for past missed prayers upon recovery.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة أوقات الصلاة كتاب الصلاة يشترط لفرضيتها ثلاثة أشياء: الإسلام والبلوغ والعقل، وتؤمر بها الأولاد لسبع سنين وتضرب عليها لعشر بيد لا بخشبة. على تركها . والصوم كالصلاة ذكورا أو إناثا وأسبابها أوقاتها، وتجب بأول الوقت وجوبا موسعاً، والأوقات خمسة وقت الصبح مبتدأ خبر أي تفترض فعلها للصلوات المفروضة خبر من طلوع الفجر الصادق إلى قبيل طلوع الشمس، ووقت الظهر من زوال الشمس إلى أن يصير ظل كل شيء مثليه أو مثله سوى ظل الاستواء، واختار الثاني الطحاوي، وهو قول الصاحبين، ووقت العصر من ابتداء الزيادة على المثل أو المثلين إلى غروب الشمس على اختلاف الروايتين كتاب الصلاة: شروع في المقصود بعد بيان الوسيلة لفرضيتها : اعلم أن الفرض نوعان: فرض عين، وفرض كفاية، ففرض العين ما يلزم كل واحد إقامته، ولا يسقط عن البعض بإقامة البعض كالإيمان ونحوه، وفرض كفاية ما يلزم جميع المسلمين إقامته ويسقط بإقامة البعض عن الباقين كالجهاد وصلاة الجنازة، والصلاة فرض عين ثبتت فرضيتها بالكتاب. [فتح القدير: ۱۹۱/۱] الإسلام فلا يفترض على كافر والبلوغ: فلا يفترض على صبي. موسعا: أي لا يأثم بالتأخير عن الجزء الأول والثاني والثالث مثلاً إثم تارك الأداء في الوقت. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٧٤] الصبح: ابتدأ ببيان وقت الفجر، وكان الأولى أن يبدأ ببيان وقت الظهر؛ لأنها أول صلاة أم فيها جبريل عليه، إلا أن وقت الفجر وقت ما اختلف في أوله وآخره تبيين الحقائق: ۲۱۳/۱] الفجر الصادق هو البياض المنتشر المستطير لا المستطيل] الفجر الثاني صادقاً؛ لأنه صدق عن الصبح وبينه، وسمي الأول كاذباً؛ لأنه يضيء، ثم يسود، ويذهب النور، ويعقبه الظلام، فكأنه كاذب تبيين الحقائق: ۲۱۳/۱] منتهى سمي زوال الشمس إلخ في معرفة الزوال روايات أصحها: أن يغرز خشبة مستوية في أرض مستوية، ويجعل عند ظلها علامة، فإن كان الظل ينقص عن العلامة فالشمس لم تزل، وإن كان الظل يطول ويجاوز الخط علم أنها زالت وإن امتنع الظل من القصر والطول، فهو وقت الزوال، كذا في "الظهيرية". [البحر الرائق: ٤٨٦/١] على المثل: فعنده: إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثليه يخرج وقت الظهر ويدخل وقت العصر، وعندهما: إذا صار ظل شيء مثله يدخل وقت العصر، فعلى هذا يكون الاختلاف في أول وقت العصر وآخر وقت الظهر، وهو ظاهر الرواية. [الكفاية: ١٩٤/١]
The Book of Prayer: Times of Prayer: The Book of Prayer: For its obligation three things are required: Islam, puberty, and sanity. Children are commanded to pray at seven years and beaten for it at ten with the hand not a stick. And fasting is like prayer, males or females. And their causes are their times, and it becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time with a broad obligation. The times are five: the time of Fajr, which is from the rising of the true dawn until just before sunrise. The time of Zuhr from the sun's zenith until the shadow of everything becomes twice its length or equal to it besides the shadow of equinox, and at-Tahawi chose the second, which is the saying of the two companions. The time of Asr from the beginning of the increase on the equal or the double until sunset according to the difference of the two narrations. The Book of Prayer: A beginning in the intended after explaining the means for its obligation. Know that the obligatory is of two types: fard ayn and fard kifayah. Fard ayn is what is required of every individual to perform, and does not fall from some by the performance of others, like faith etc. Fard kifayah is what is required of all Muslims to perform and falls with the performance of some from the rest, like jihad and funeral prayer. And prayer is fard ayn, its obligation established by the Book. [Fath al-Qadir: 191/1] Islam: so it is not obligatory upon a disbeliever. Puberty: so it is not obligatory upon a child. Broad: meaning one does not sin by delaying the first part, second, third, etc., like the sin of the one who leaves performance in the time. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 174] Fajr: He began by explaining the time of Fajr, but it would have been more appropriate to begin with the time of Zuhr because it was the first prayer that Jibril (peace be upon him) led, except that the time of Fajr is a time where there is dispute about its beginning and end. Tabayin al-Haqaiq: 213/1] The true dawn is the spreading horizontal whiteness, not the vertical. The second dawn is called truthful because it gives truth to the morning and clarifies it, and the first is called false because it gives light then darkens, the light goes and darkness follows, so it is as if false. Tabayin al-Haqaiq: 213/1] The end is called the zenith of the sun etc. Regarding knowing the zenith, the most authentic report is to plant a straight stick in level ground, and place a mark at its shadow. If the shadow decreases from the mark, the sun has not passed the zenith. If the shadow increases and exceeds the line, know that it has passed. If the shadow does not shorten or lengthen, it is the time of zenith. This is in al-Dhahiriyya. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 486/1] On the equal: According to him (Abu Hanifa): when the shadow of everything becomes twice its length, Zuhr time exits and Asr time enters. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): when the shadow of something becomes equal to it, Asr time enters. So the difference is in the beginning of Asr and the end of Zuhr, and this is the apparent narration. [Al-Kifaya: 194/1]
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah begins the Book of Prayer (Kitab al-Salah) by establishing the conditions for its obligation: Islam, puberty, and sanity. Children are instructed to pray from age seven and disciplined at ten. The obligation of prayer is a fard ayn, individually obligatory, established by the Quran. The 'causes' of prayer are its times, and the obligation becomes binding at the start of the time in a broad sense (wujub musa'), meaning delaying within the time does not incur sin. The five times are then described: Fajr from true dawn to just before sunrise; Zuhr from zenith until the shadow of an object becomes twice its length (or equal, with preference for the latter according to al-Tahawi, which is the view of the two Sahibayn); Asr from when the shadow exceeds the chosen measure until sunset, with two narrations. The commentary explains the types of fard, the definitions of true and false dawn, and the method for determining zenith. It also details the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the end of Zuhr and beginning of Asr: Abu Hanifa uses the double shadow, while the two Sahibayn use the equal shadow.

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard ayn): Individual obligation that every Muslim must perform personally, e.g., daily prayers.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): Communal obligation that falls from the rest when sufficient Muslims perform it, e.g., funeral prayer.
وجوب موسع (wujub musa'): Broad obligation: the obligation is established at the beginning of the time but can be performed any time within the period without sin for delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the obligation of prayer according to this passage?
A) Being male
B) Being wealthy
C) Having reached puberty
D) Being in a state of purity

Key Takeaway
Prayer is obligatory only on Muslims who are sane and have reached puberty; children are trained but not obligated.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Times of Prayer: Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr
Defines times of Fajr, Zuhr, Asr and presents intra-Hanafi dispute on Asr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the time periods for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr prayers according to the Hanafi school, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the beginning of Asr time.

Core Idea
Asr time begins when a shadow equals the object's height, according to the preferred view of the Sahibayn.

After establishing conditions, the text defines the times of prayer, which are the 'causes' (asbab) that trigger the obligation. The definitions for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr are given, with a notable internal dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions on when Zuhr ends and Asr begins. Understanding these times is essential for performing prayers on schedule.

Guided Path
1
Understand wujub musa'
The obligation to pray enters at the beginning of the time, but one may delay within the entire period without sin. This is called 'wujub musa''.
This is specific to prayers; other obligations like fasting have fixed times.
2
Define Fajr time
Fajr begins at true dawn (fajr sadiq) – the spreading whiteness on the horizon – and ends just before sunrise. The false dawn (fajr kadhib) is not valid.
The commentary explains the two dawns: false dawn is vertical and then darkens; true dawn is horizontal and increases.
3
Define Zuhr time
Zuhr begins when the sun passes its zenith (zawal) and ends when the shadow of an object becomes either twice its height (Abu Hanifa) or equal to its height (Sahibayn), excluding the shadow at zenith.
The text gives two measures, and at-Tahawi preferred the Sahibayn's equal shadow.
4
Analyze the Asr dispute
Asr time begins immediately after Zuhr ends. Thus: Abu Hanifa says Asr starts when shadow is double; Sahibayn say when shadow is equal. The difference is in the beginning of Asr and the end of Zuhr.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is the Sahibayn's view (equal shadow).
5
Note the practical difference
If at a given moment shadow equals object height, according to Abu Hanifa Zuhr time is still ongoing; according to Sahibayn Asr has entered. A follower should follow the mufta bihi view.
The same difference applies to the end of Asr? No, Asr ends at sunset for both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة أوقات الصلاة كتاب الصلاة يشترط لفرضيتها ثلاثة أشياء: الإسلام والبلوغ والعقل، وتؤمر بها الأولاد لسبع سنين وتضرب عليها لعشر بيد لا بخشبة. على تركها . والصوم كالصلاة ذكورا أو إناثا وأسبابها أوقاتها، وتجب بأول الوقت وجوبا موسعاً، والأوقات خمسة وقت الصبح مبتدأ خبر أي تفترض فعلها للصلوات المفروضة خبر من طلوع الفجر الصادق إلى قبيل طلوع الشمس، ووقت الظهر من زوال الشمس إلى أن يصير ظل كل شيء مثليه أو مثله سوى ظل الاستواء، واختار الثاني الطحاوي، وهو قول الصاحبين، ووقت العصر من ابتداء الزيادة على المثل أو المثلين إلى غروب الشمس على اختلاف الروايتين كتاب الصلاة: شروع في المقصود بعد بيان الوسيلة لفرضيتها : اعلم أن الفرض نوعان: فرض عين، وفرض كفاية، ففرض العين ما يلزم كل واحد إقامته، ولا يسقط عن البعض بإقامة البعض كالإيمان ونحوه، وفرض كفاية ما يلزم جميع المسلمين إقامته ويسقط بإقامة البعض عن الباقين كالجهاد وصلاة الجنازة، والصلاة فرض عين ثبتت فرضيتها بالكتاب. [فتح القدير: ۱۹۱/۱] الإسلام فلا يفترض على كافر والبلوغ: فلا يفترض على صبي. موسعا: أي لا يأثم بالتأخير عن الجزء الأول والثاني والثالث مثلاً إثم تارك الأداء في الوقت. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ١٧٤] الصبح: ابتدأ ببيان وقت الفجر، وكان الأولى أن يبدأ ببيان وقت الظهر؛ لأنها أول صلاة أم فيها جبريل عليه، إلا أن وقت الفجر وقت ما اختلف في أوله وآخره تبيين الحقائق: ۲۱۳/۱] الفجر الصادق هو البياض المنتشر المستطير لا المستطيل] الفجر الثاني صادقاً؛ لأنه صدق عن الصبح وبينه، وسمي الأول كاذباً؛ لأنه يضيء، ثم يسود، ويذهب النور، ويعقبه الظلام، فكأنه كاذب تبيين الحقائق: ۲۱۳/۱] منتهى سمي زوال الشمس إلخ في معرفة الزوال روايات أصحها: أن يغرز خشبة مستوية في أرض مستوية، ويجعل عند ظلها علامة، فإن كان الظل ينقص عن العلامة فالشمس لم تزل، وإن كان الظل يطول ويجاوز الخط علم أنها زالت وإن امتنع الظل من القصر والطول، فهو وقت الزوال، كذا في "الظهيرية". [البحر الرائق: ٤٨٦/١] على المثل: فعنده: إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثليه يخرج وقت الظهر ويدخل وقت العصر، وعندهما: إذا صار ظل شيء مثله يدخل وقت العصر، فعلى هذا يكون الاختلاف في أول وقت العصر وآخر وقت الظهر، وهو ظاهر الرواية. [الكفاية: ١٩٤/١]
The Book of Prayer: Times of Prayer: The Book of Prayer: For its obligation three things are required: Islam, puberty, and sanity. Children are commanded to pray at seven years and beaten for it at ten with the hand not a stick. And fasting is like prayer, males or females. And their causes are their times, and it becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time with a broad obligation. The times are five: the time of Fajr, which is from the rising of the true dawn until just before sunrise. The time of Zuhr from the sun's zenith until the shadow of everything becomes twice its length or equal to it besides the shadow of equinox, and at-Tahawi chose the second, which is the saying of the two companions. The time of Asr from the beginning of the increase on the equal or the double until sunset according to the difference of the two narrations. The Book of Prayer: A beginning in the intended after explaining the means for its obligation. Know that the obligatory is of two types: fard ayn and fard kifayah. Fard ayn is what is required of every individual to perform, and does not fall from some by the performance of others, like faith etc. Fard kifayah is what is required of all Muslims to perform and falls with the performance of some from the rest, like jihad and funeral prayer. And prayer is fard ayn, its obligation established by the Book. [Fath al-Qadir: 191/1] Islam: so it is not obligatory upon a disbeliever. Puberty: so it is not obligatory upon a child. Broad: meaning one does not sin by delaying the first part, second, third, etc., like the sin of the one who leaves performance in the time. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 174] Fajr: He began by explaining the time of Fajr, but it would have been more appropriate to begin with the time of Zuhr because it was the first prayer that Jibril (peace be upon him) led, except that the time of Fajr is a time where there is dispute about its beginning and end. Tabayin al-Haqaiq: 213/1] The true dawn is the spreading horizontal whiteness, not the vertical. The second dawn is called truthful because it gives truth to the morning and clarifies it, and the first is called false because it gives light then darkens, the light goes and darkness follows, so it is as if false. Tabayin al-Haqaiq: 213/1] The end is called the zenith of the sun etc. Regarding knowing the zenith, the most authentic report is to plant a straight stick in level ground, and place a mark at its shadow. If the shadow decreases from the mark, the sun has not passed the zenith. If the shadow increases and exceeds the line, know that it has passed. If the shadow does not shorten or lengthen, it is the time of zenith. This is in al-Dhahiriyya. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 486/1] On the equal: According to him (Abu Hanifa): when the shadow of everything becomes twice its length, Zuhr time exits and Asr time enters. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): when the shadow of something becomes equal to it, Asr time enters. So the difference is in the beginning of Asr and the end of Zuhr, and this is the apparent narration. [Al-Kifaya: 194/1]
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah begins the Book of Prayer (Kitab al-Salah) by establishing the conditions for its obligation: Islam, puberty, and sanity. Children are instructed to pray from age seven and disciplined at ten. The obligation of prayer is a fard ayn, individually obligatory, established by the Quran. The 'causes' of prayer are its times, and the obligation becomes binding at the start of the time in a broad sense (wujub musa'), meaning delaying within the time does not incur sin. The five times are then described: Fajr from true dawn to just before sunrise; Zuhr from zenith until the shadow of an object becomes twice its length (or equal, with preference for the latter according to al-Tahawi, which is the view of the two Sahibayn); Asr from when the shadow exceeds the chosen measure until sunset, with two narrations. The commentary explains the types of fard, the definitions of true and false dawn, and the method for determining zenith. It also details the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the end of Zuhr and beginning of Asr: Abu Hanifa uses the double shadow, while the two Sahibayn use the equal shadow.

Key Terms
فجر صادق (fajr sadiq): The true dawn: the spreading whiteness that signals the start of Fajr time.
زوال الشمس (zawal al-shams): The sun's zenith: when it reaches the highest point and shadows begin to lengthen.
مثل ومثلي (mithl wa mithlayn): Equal shadow and double shadow; measures for Zuhr and Asr timings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following best describes the beginning of Asr time?
A) When the shadow of an object is twice its height.
B) When the shadow of an object equals its height, according to the mufta bihi.
C) When the sun is at its zenith.
D) When the red twilight disappears.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school for Asr time is the Sahibayn's view: Asr enters when an object's shadow equals its height.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Times of Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr with Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Shadow Lengths
Explains conditions for prayer obligation and times of Fajr, Zuhr, Asr with intra-Hanafi dispute on shadow lengths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for prayer obligation, identify the times of Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr according to the Hanafi school, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the shadow length for Asr.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school agrees on prayer times but splits on when Asr begins: Abu Hanifa says double shadow, Sahibayn say equal shadow.

This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the prerequisites for prayer being obligatory and then defines the five prayer times. A key intra-Hanafi dispute appears in the definition of Zuhr's end and Asr's start: whether the shadow must be twice the object's height or just equal to it. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how different ijtihad can coexist within one school.

Guided Path
1
Identify conditions for prayer obligation
Extract the three conditions (Islam, puberty, reason) and note the ruling for children (command at 7, discipline at 10).
These are shurut for wujoob (obligation), not for validity.
2
Define the time for Fajr
Note that Fajr begins at true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) and ends just before sunrise. The true dawn is the horizontal spreading whiteness.
Distinguish from false dawn.
3
Analyze the dispute on Zuhr and Asr times
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa says Zuhr ends when shadow is twice object's height; Sahibayn say when shadow is equal to height. Note that the text chooses the Sahibayn's view as mufta bihi.
The difference is in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah).
4
Understand the practical consequence
Recognize that according to the mufta bihi, Asr begins earlier (equal shadow), so Zuhr time is shorter compared to Abu Hanifa's view.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the actual beginning of Asr prayer time.

كل
Book of Prayer. 70. Times of Prayer. Book of Prayer. Three things are conditions for its obligation: Islam, puberty, and reason. Children are commanded to pray at seven years and beaten for it at ten with a hand not a stick. The responsibility of a person includes leaving it. Fasting is like prayer, males or females. Its causes are its times. It becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time with a broad obligation (wujoob musa'). The times are five: the time of Fajr begins from the rising of the true dawn until just before sunrise; the time of Zuhr from the sun's zenith until the shadow of everything becomes twice its length or once its length besides the shadow of noon, and al-Tahawi chose the second, which is the saying of the two companions; the time of Asr from the beginning of the increase over the one or double shadow to sunset, according to the difference of the two narrations. Book of Prayer: Beginning in the intended after explaining the means for its obligation: Know that obligation is two types: individual obligation (fard 'ayn) and collective obligation (fard kifaya). Fard 'ayn is what is required of each individual to perform, and it is not dropped from some by the performance of others, like faith and similar. Fard kifaya is what is required of all Muslims to perform and is dropped by the performance of some from the rest, like jihad and funeral prayer. Prayer is fard 'ayn, its obligation established by the Book. [Fath al-Qadir 1/191] Islam: it is not obligated upon a disbeliever. Puberty: it is not obligated upon a child. Broadly: i.e., one is not sinful for delaying from the first, second, and third parts, for example, like the sin of abandoning performance within the time. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 174] Fajr: He began by explaining the time of dawn, although it would have been better to begin by explaining the time of Zuhr, because it was the first prayer in which Jibril (peace be upon him) led him, except that the time of Fajr is a time whose beginning and end were disputed. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/213] The true dawn is the spreading, widespread whiteness, not the elongated. The second dawn is called true because it is truthful about the morning and makes it clear; the first is called false because it shines, then darkens, the light goes, and darkness follows, so it is as if it is false. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/213] The end. It is called. The sun's zenith etc. Regarding knowing the zenith, there are narrations, the most authentic: that one inserts a straight stick into level ground, and places a marker at its shadow. If the shadow decreases from the marker, the sun has not yet declined; if the shadow lengthens and exceeds the line, it is known that it has declined; and if the shadow refrains from decreasing and increasing, it is the time of zenith. Thus in al-Dhahiriyyah. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/486] Regarding the one shadow: According to him (Abu Hanifa), when the shadow of everything becomes twice its length, the time of Zuhr ends and the time of Asr enters. According to them (the two companions), when the shadow of a thing becomes its length, the time of Asr enters. So this is the difference in the beginning of Asr and the end of Zuhr, and it is the apparent narration. [Al-Kifaya 1/194] Everything.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Salah covers the conditions for the obligation of prayer and the times of Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr. It begins by stating that prayer becomes obligatory upon a person who is Muslim, has reached puberty, and is sane. Children are instructed to pray at age seven and disciplined at ten, but the obligation is not upon them. Then it lists the five prayer times, focusing on Fajr (from true dawn to just before sunrise), Zuhr (from zenith until the shadow of everything is twice its length [Abu Hanifa] or once its length [Sahibayn] beyond the noon shadow), and Asr (from the increase over the one or double shadow until sunset). The commentary explains that the choice of the second view (once the length) is attributed to al-Tahawi and is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn). This creates an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa says Asr enters when the shadow is twice the object's height, while the Sahibayn say when it is once the height. The text notes that this difference is in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The passage also defines the true dawn and describes a method to determine the sun's zenith using a vertical stick. Overall, it provides a detailed ruling on the time boundaries for these prayers.

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation that every responsible Muslim must perform personally.
وجوب موسع (wujoob musa'): An obligation that is broad or expanded, meaning one may delay performing it within the time without sin as long as it is done before the time expires.
الفجر الصادق (al-fajr al-sadiq): The true dawn, which is the spreading horizontal whiteness on the horizon that signals the beginning of Fajr prayer time.
المثل والمثليه (al-mithl wa al-mithlayn): The shadow length being equal to the object's height (mithl) or twice the height (mithlayn) beyond the noon shadow, used to determine the end of Zuhr and beginning of Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, when does the time of Asr begin?
A) When the shadow of an object is twice its length
B) When the shadow of an object is equal to its length
C) When the shadow of an object is half its length
D) When the sun begins to decline from its zenith

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two authentic narrations on the shadow length for Asr, but the preferred fatwa follows the Sahibayn (equal shadow).

The Shafaq Dispute and End of Maghrib Time
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shafaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the definition of shafaq and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight, though Abu Hanifa's whiteness view is noted.

Prayer times are pillars of validity. For Maghrib, the moment the twilight fades signals its end. But what exactly is 'shafaq'? The Hanafi school has a well-known internal disagreement that affects the length of Maghrib time. This lesson unpacks the positions and the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed starting point
All Hanafi scholars agree that Maghrib time ends at the disappearance of shafaq (twilight). The dispute is only over what shafaq means.
2
State the position of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) held that shafaq is the redness (al-humrah) that appears after sunset.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the school.
3
State the position of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa originally defined shafaq as the whiteness (al-bayad) that follows the redness, making Maghrib time longer.
He is reported to have retracted to the Sahibayn's view.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is the redness view, though some later scholars like Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq preferred Abu Hanifa's original view.
In practice, Hanafi fatwas follow the redness.
5
Apply the ruling
Therefore, Maghrib time ends when the red glow in the sky disappears. If one delays until after that, the prayer becomes qada.
This has practical consequences for the start of Isha time.

Source Text

والمغرب منه إلى غروب الشفق الأحمر على المفتى به والعشاء والوتر منه إلى الصبح، الصادق إجماعاً ولا يقدم الوتر على العشاء للترتيب اللازم ومن لم يجد وقتهما لم يجبا عليه، ولا يجمع بين فرضين في وقت بعذر إلا في عرفة للحاج بشرط الإمام الأعظم والإحرام، فيجمع بين الظهر والعصر جمع تقديم، ويجمع بين المغرب والعشاء بمزدلفة هو في وقت الظهر الشفق: اعلم أنهم اتفقوا على أن منتهى وقت المغرب إلى الشفق، ولكن اختلفوا في تفسير الشفق، فقالا: الشفق الحمرة، وإليه يروى رجوع أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو حنيفة: الشفق هو البياض الذي بعد الحمرة، فوقت المغرب أزيد عند أبي حنيفة منه عندهما، ورجح في البحر قول الإمام والعشاء: أي ابتداء وقت صلاة العشاء والوتر من غروب الشفق على الاختلاف الذي تقدم إلى قبيل طلوع الصبح الصادق؛ لإجماع السلف. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۷۸] لا يقدم الوتر إلخ أطلقه وهو مقيد بالتذكر كما هو مذكور في "البداية"، فلو قدم الوتر على العشاء ناسيا لا يعيد الوتر، وكذا لو صلى العشاء بغير طهارة ثم نام فقام وتوضأ وصلى الوتر، ثم تذكر أنه صلى العشاء بغير طهارة، يعيدها دون الوتر فيهما. للترتيب اللازم أي لا يقدم الوتر على العشاء؛ لوجوب الترتيب اللازم بين العشاء والوتر، وهذا جواب عن سؤال مقدر تقريره لم لا يجوز تقديمه بعد دخول وقته؟ أجاب بأنه إنما لا يجوز؛ للترتيب، لا لكون الوقت لم يدخل، وهذا على قوله، وعلى قولهما؛ لأنه تبع للعشاء، وأثر الخلاف يظهر فيما لو قدم الوتر عليها ناسياً أو تذكر أنه صلاها فقط على غير وضوء لا يعيده عنده وعندهما يعيد [رد المحتار: ٣٦١/١] ومن لم يجد إلخ أي من لم يجد وقت العشاء والوتر بأن كان في بلد يطلع الفجر كما تغرب الشمس، أو قبل أن يغيب الشفق لم يجبا عليه؛ لعدم السبب، وهو الوقت ولا يجمع إلخ أي لا يجوز الجمع بين فرضين في وقت واحد ولو كان لعذر ، إلا في عرفة للحاج، لا لغيرهم بشرط أن يصلي الحاج مع الإمام الأعظم أي السلطان أو نائبه كلا من الظهر والعصر، بشرط الإحرام بحج، لا عمرة، حال صلاة كل من الظهر والعصر ولو أحرم بعد الزوال في الصحيح، وصحة الظهر، فلو تبين فساده ،أعاده ويعيد العصر إذا دخل وقته المعتاد، فهذه أربعة شروط لصحة الجمع عند الإمام، أولها ،عرفة وثانيها صحة الظهر، وثالثها الإمام أو نائبه، ورابعها: الإحرام بالحج. واحترز بقوله: "في وقت" عن الجمع بينهما فعلاً بأن صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها، بأن يصلي الأولى في آخر وقتها، والثانية في أول وقتها، فإنه جمع في حق الفعل وإن لم يكن جمعاً في حق الوقت. (مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي، الزيلعي بزيادة فيجمع إلخ بأذان واحد وإقامتين. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٨٠] ويجمع إلخ بأذان واحد وإقامة واحدة. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۸۰]
And Maghrib from it to the disappearance of the red twilight (ash-shafaq al-ahmar) according to the fatwa. And Isha and Witr from it to the true dawn by consensus. And Witr is not performed before Isha due to the necessary order. And whoever does not find their time [i.e., Isha and Witr] is not obligated for them. And one does not combine two obligatory prayers in one time due to an excuse except at Arafah for the pilgrim with the condition of the supreme imam and ihram. So he combines Zuhr and Asr as an advance combination (jam' taqdim), and he combines Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. He is in the time of Zuhr. The twilight (shafaq): Know that they agreed that the end of Maghrib time is at the twilight, but they differed in interpreting the twilight. They (the two companions) said: the twilight is the redness, and it is narrated that Abu Hanifa retracted to this. And Abu Hanifa said: the twilight is the whiteness that comes after the redness, so Maghrib time is longer according to Abu Hanifa than according to them. And in Al-Bahr, the saying of the Imam is preferred. And Isha: i.e., the beginning of the time of Isha and Witr is from the disappearance of the twilight according to the difference mentioned previously to just before the rising of the true dawn, due to the consensus of the Salaf. [Maraqi al-Falah 178] 'He does not advance Witr' etc. He made it absolute, but it is restricted by memory as mentioned in Al-Bidayah. So if one advances Witr before Isha forgetfully, he does not repeat Witr. Similarly, if one prays Isha without purification, then sleeps, then gets up, performs ablution, and prays Witr, then remembers that he prayed Isha without purification, he repeats Isha but not Witr in both cases. Due to the necessary order, i.e., Witr is not advanced before Isha because of the necessity of the order between Isha and Witr. This is a response to an implied question: why is it not permissible to advance it after its time has entered? He answered that it is not permissible due to order, not because the time has not entered. This is according to his (Abu Hanifa's) saying and according to theirs (the two companions') because it is a follower of Isha. The effect of the difference appears if one advances it before it forgetfully or remembers that he prayed it only without wudu; he does not repeat it according to him (Abu Hanifa) but according to them he repeats. [Radd al-Muhtar 1/361] And whoever does not find etc., i.e., whoever does not find the time of Isha and Witr, such as being in a land where dawn rises at sunset or before the twilight disappears, they are not obligated for them due to the absence of the cause, which is the time. And one does not combine etc., i.e., it is not permissible to combine two obligatory prayers in one time even due to an excuse, except at Arafah for the pilgrim, not for others, with the condition that the pilgrim prays with the supreme imam, i.e., the sultan or his deputy, both Zuhr and Asr, with the condition of ihram for Hajj, not for Umrah, at the time of each of Zuhr and Asr, even if he entered ihram after noon according to the correct view, and the validity of Zuhr; so if it becomes apparent that it was invalid, he repeats it and repeats Asr if its usual time has entered. So these are four conditions for the validity of combining according to the Imam: first, Arafah; second, validity of Zuhr; third, the imam or his deputy; fourth, ihram for Hajj. And he guarded by saying 'in a time' against combining between them in action, such that he prays each in its own time by praying the first at the end of its time and the second at the beginning of its time; this is combining in action though not in time. (Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, al-Zayla'i with addition: 'so he combines etc. with one adhan and two iqamas' [Maraqi al-Falah 180]; 'and he combines etc. with one adhan and one iqama' [Maraqi al-Falah 180].)
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of prayer times, focusing on Maghrib, Isha, and Witr, followed by rules on combining prayers (jam'). For Maghrib, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the Sahibayn define 'shafaq' as the redness in the western sky, while Abu Hanifa initially defined it as the whiteness after redness, but he is reported to have retracted to the view of the Sahibayn. According to the mufta bihi (fatwa), Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight. Isha and Witr then begin from that point until true dawn, by consensus. The passage emphasizes that Witr must follow Isha in order; it cannot be advanced before Isha. However, if someone forgetfully prays Witr before Isha, they do not repeat Witr if they later remember, according to Abu Hanifa (differently from the Sahibayn). Then the passage discusses the prohibition of combining two obligatory prayers in one time, except at Arafah and Muzdalifah for a pilgrim performing Hajj. At Arafah, one combines Zuhr and Asr in the time of Zuhr with advance combination (jam' taqdim), with specific conditions: being present at Arafah, praying with the supreme imam (or his deputy), being in the state of ihram for Hajj, and having a valid Zuhr prayer. At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are combined in the time of Isha with delay (jam' ta'khir). The passage also clarifies that combining in action (praying each at its own time but near each other) is not considered combining in time and is prohibited without the specified exceptions.

Key Terms
الشفق (ash-shafaq): The twilight after sunset: either the redness (Sahibayn, mufta bihi) or the whiteness after redness (Abu Hanifa). Its disappearance marks the end of Maghrib time.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon position for issuing fatwas; here it is the view of the Sahibayn (redness).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi definition of shafaq in the Hanafi school?
A) The whiteness after redness
B) The redness after sunset
C) The total darkness
D) The light before dawn

Key Takeaway
Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight, following the mufta bihi, though alternative views exist within the school.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Necessary Order Between Isha and Witr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the necessity of repeating Witr when order is forgotten

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that Witr must be prayed after Isha and distinguish the consequences if the order is forgotten.

Core Idea
Witr must follow Isha; if forgotten, Witr is not repeated according to Abu Hanifa.

Witr holds a special status in the Hanafi school as a wajib prayer. But its timing is inseparably tied to Isha: it must come after the Isha prayer. This lesson explores the necessary order (tartib lazim) and the practical rulings if someone accidentally reverses them.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Witr cannot be prayed before Isha even if its time has entered. This is due to the necessary order (tartib lazim) between the two.
The order is wajib, not due to time but due to sequence.
2
Identify the exceptional case of forgetfulness
If a person forgetfully prays Witr before Isha, according to Abu Hanifa, he does not repeat Witr. According to the Sahibayn, he must repeat it.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze another scenario: praying Isha without wudu then later remembering
If one prays Isha without wudu, then later prays Witr, then remembers, he repeats Isha but not Witr according to Abu Hanifa.
This shows Witr's validity is not conditioned on Isha's validity according to Abu Hanifa.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa is on the view of Abu Hanifa: Witr is not repeated if the order is forgotten.
The text mentions 'Radd al-Muhtar' supports this.
5
Apply to real situations
If someone mistakenly prays Witr before Isha, they should still pray Isha afterwards, but do not need to repeat Witr.
This avoids unnecessary repetition.

الترتيب اللازم (at-tartib al-lazim): The necessary order between Isha and Witr: Witr must be prayed after Isha, not before.
ناسياً (nasiyan): Forgetfully; the ruling on the order changes if done intentionally vs forgetfully.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Combining Prayers: Only at Arafah and Muzdalifah
Ruling with conditions on combining prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions for combining prayers at Arafah and Muzdalifah and explain why it is prohibited elsewhere.

Core Idea
Combining obligatory prayers is strictly forbidden except for a Hajj pilgrim at Arafah and Muzdalifah with specific conditions.

While many schools allow combining prayers during travel or illness, the Hanafi school restricts it to the two sacred locations during Hajj. This lesson dissects the conditions for the exception and clarifies the difference between combining in time versus combining in action.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
It is not permissible to combine two obligatory prayers at one time for any excuse, except at Arafah and Muzdalifah for a Hajj pilgrim.
This is the Hanafi position; it is more restrictive than other schools.
2
Identify the type of combining at Arafah
At Arafah, Zuhr and Asr are combined with advance combination (jam' taqdim) in the time of Zuhr.
The pilgrim prays both during Zuhr time.
3
Identify the type at Muzdalifah
At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are combined with delay (jam' ta'khir) in the time of Isha.
The pilgrim delays Maghrib until Isha time.
4
List the conditions for Arafah
Four conditions: being at Arafah, validity of Zuhr prayer, presence of the supreme imam or his deputy, and being in ihram for Hajj (not Umrah).
These are from the text and commentary.
5
Distinguish combining in time from combining in action
Combining in action (praying one at the end of its time and the next at the beginning) is not considered true combining and is not permitted without the specific excuse.
This prevents loopholes.

والمغرب منه إلى غروب الشفق الأحمر على المفتى به والعشاء والوتر منه إلى الصبح، الصادق إجماعاً ولا يقدم الوتر على العشاء للترتيب اللازم ومن لم يجد وقتهما لم يجبا عليه، ولا يجمع بين فرضين في وقت بعذر إلا في عرفة للحاج بشرط الإمام الأعظم والإحرام، فيجمع بين الظهر والعصر جمع تقديم، ويجمع بين المغرب والعشاء بمزدلفة هو في وقت الظهر الشفق: اعلم أنهم اتفقوا على أن منتهى وقت المغرب إلى الشفق، ولكن اختلفوا في تفسير الشفق، فقالا: الشفق الحمرة، وإليه يروى رجوع أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو حنيفة: الشفق هو البياض الذي بعد الحمرة، فوقت المغرب أزيد عند أبي حنيفة منه عندهما، ورجح في البحر قول الإمام والعشاء: أي ابتداء وقت صلاة العشاء والوتر من غروب الشفق على الاختلاف الذي تقدم إلى قبيل طلوع الصبح الصادق؛ لإجماع السلف. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۷۸] لا يقدم الوتر إلخ أطلقه وهو مقيد بالتذكر كما هو مذكور في "البداية"، فلو قدم الوتر على العشاء ناسيا لا يعيد الوتر، وكذا لو صلى العشاء بغير طهارة ثم نام فقام وتوضأ وصلى الوتر، ثم تذكر أنه صلى العشاء بغير طهارة، يعيدها دون الوتر فيهما. للترتيب اللازم أي لا يقدم الوتر على العشاء؛ لوجوب الترتيب اللازم بين العشاء والوتر، وهذا جواب عن سؤال مقدر تقريره لم لا يجوز تقديمه بعد دخول وقته؟ أجاب بأنه إنما لا يجوز؛ للترتيب، لا لكون الوقت لم يدخل، وهذا على قوله، وعلى قولهما؛ لأنه تبع للعشاء، وأثر الخلاف يظهر فيما لو قدم الوتر عليها ناسياً أو تذكر أنه صلاها فقط على غير وضوء لا يعيده عنده وعندهما يعيد [رد المحتار: ٣٦١/١] ومن لم يجد إلخ أي من لم يجد وقت العشاء والوتر بأن كان في بلد يطلع الفجر كما تغرب الشمس، أو قبل أن يغيب الشفق لم يجبا عليه؛ لعدم السبب، وهو الوقت ولا يجمع إلخ أي لا يجوز الجمع بين فرضين في وقت واحد ولو كان لعذر ، إلا في عرفة للحاج، لا لغيرهم بشرط أن يصلي الحاج مع الإمام الأعظم أي السلطان أو نائبه كلا من الظهر والعصر، بشرط الإحرام بحج، لا عمرة، حال صلاة كل من الظهر والعصر ولو أحرم بعد الزوال في الصحيح، وصحة الظهر، فلو تبين فساده ،أعاده ويعيد العصر إذا دخل وقته المعتاد، فهذه أربعة شروط لصحة الجمع عند الإمام، أولها ،عرفة وثانيها صحة الظهر، وثالثها الإمام أو نائبه، ورابعها: الإحرام بالحج. واحترز بقوله: "في وقت" عن الجمع بينهما فعلاً بأن صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها، بأن يصلي الأولى في آخر وقتها، والثانية في أول وقتها، فإنه جمع في حق الفعل وإن لم يكن جمعاً في حق الوقت. (مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي، الزيلعي بزيادة فيجمع إلخ بأذان واحد وإقامتين. [مراقي الفلاح: ١٨٠] ويجمع إلخ بأذان واحد وإقامة واحدة. [مراقي الفلاح: ۱۸۰]
And Maghrib from it to the disappearance of the red twilight (ash-shafaq al-ahmar) according to the fatwa. And Isha and Witr from it to the true dawn by consensus. And Witr is not performed before Isha due to the necessary order. And whoever does not find their time [i.e., Isha and Witr] is not obligated for them. And one does not combine two obligatory prayers in one time due to an excuse except at Arafah for the pilgrim with the condition of the supreme imam and ihram. So he combines Zuhr and Asr as an advance combination (jam' taqdim), and he combines Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. He is in the time of Zuhr. The twilight (shafaq): Know that they agreed that the end of Maghrib time is at the twilight, but they differed in interpreting the twilight. They (the two companions) said: the twilight is the redness, and it is narrated that Abu Hanifa retracted to this. And Abu Hanifa said: the twilight is the whiteness that comes after the redness, so Maghrib time is longer according to Abu Hanifa than according to them. And in Al-Bahr, the saying of the Imam is preferred. And Isha: i.e., the beginning of the time of Isha and Witr is from the disappearance of the twilight according to the difference mentioned previously to just before the rising of the true dawn, due to the consensus of the Salaf. [Maraqi al-Falah 178] 'He does not advance Witr' etc. He made it absolute, but it is restricted by memory as mentioned in Al-Bidayah. So if one advances Witr before Isha forgetfully, he does not repeat Witr. Similarly, if one prays Isha without purification, then sleeps, then gets up, performs ablution, and prays Witr, then remembers that he prayed Isha without purification, he repeats Isha but not Witr in both cases. Due to the necessary order, i.e., Witr is not advanced before Isha because of the necessity of the order between Isha and Witr. This is a response to an implied question: why is it not permissible to advance it after its time has entered? He answered that it is not permissible due to order, not because the time has not entered. This is according to his (Abu Hanifa's) saying and according to theirs (the two companions') because it is a follower of Isha. The effect of the difference appears if one advances it before it forgetfully or remembers that he prayed it only without wudu; he does not repeat it according to him (Abu Hanifa) but according to them he repeats. [Radd al-Muhtar 1/361] And whoever does not find etc., i.e., whoever does not find the time of Isha and Witr, such as being in a land where dawn rises at sunset or before the twilight disappears, they are not obligated for them due to the absence of the cause, which is the time. And one does not combine etc., i.e., it is not permissible to combine two obligatory prayers in one time even due to an excuse, except at Arafah for the pilgrim, not for others, with the condition that the pilgrim prays with the supreme imam, i.e., the sultan or his deputy, both Zuhr and Asr, with the condition of ihram for Hajj, not for Umrah, at the time of each of Zuhr and Asr, even if he entered ihram after noon according to the correct view, and the validity of Zuhr; so if it becomes apparent that it was invalid, he repeats it and repeats Asr if its usual time has entered. So these are four conditions for the validity of combining according to the Imam: first, Arafah; second, validity of Zuhr; third, the imam or his deputy; fourth, ihram for Hajj. And he guarded by saying 'in a time' against combining between them in action, such that he prays each in its own time by praying the first at the end of its time and the second at the beginning of its time; this is combining in action though not in time. (Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, al-Zayla'i with addition: 'so he combines etc. with one adhan and two iqamas' [Maraqi al-Falah 180]; 'and he combines etc. with one adhan and one iqama' [Maraqi al-Falah 180].)
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of prayer times, focusing on Maghrib, Isha, and Witr, followed by rules on combining prayers (jam'). For Maghrib, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the Sahibayn define 'shafaq' as the redness in the western sky, while Abu Hanifa initially defined it as the whiteness after redness, but he is reported to have retracted to the view of the Sahibayn. According to the mufta bihi (fatwa), Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight. Isha and Witr then begin from that point until true dawn, by consensus. The passage emphasizes that Witr must follow Isha in order; it cannot be advanced before Isha. However, if someone forgetfully prays Witr before Isha, they do not repeat Witr if they later remember, according to Abu Hanifa (differently from the Sahibayn). Then the passage discusses the prohibition of combining two obligatory prayers in one time, except at Arafah and Muzdalifah for a pilgrim performing Hajj. At Arafah, one combines Zuhr and Asr in the time of Zuhr with advance combination (jam' taqdim), with specific conditions: being present at Arafah, praying with the supreme imam (or his deputy), being in the state of ihram for Hajj, and having a valid Zuhr prayer. At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are combined in the time of Isha with delay (jam' ta'khir). The passage also clarifies that combining in action (praying each at its own time but near each other) is not considered combining in time and is prohibited without the specified exceptions.

Key Terms
جمع التقديم (jam' at-taqdim): Combining two prayers by performing both in the time of the earlier prayer (e.g., Zuhr and Asr at Zuhr time).
الإمام الأعظم (al-imam al-a'zam): The supreme imam, i.e., the ruler or his deputy; a condition for combining at Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Both in the time of Isha (delay)
D) Each in its own time but back-to-back

Key Takeaway
Combining obligatory prayers is prohibited except for a Hajj pilgrim at Arafah (advance) and Muzdalifah (delay) with specific conditions.

The Necessary Order Between Isha and Witr
States the rule of order and exceptions for forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order between Isha and Witr, distinguish the intra-madhhab disagreement on forgetfulness, and apply the exception for indefinite times.

Core Idea
Witr must be after Isha; if forgotten, Abu Hanifa holds Witr valid, the Sahibayn require repetition.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies the necessary order (al-tartib al-lazim) between Isha and Witr. While the order is wajib, the text addresses the case of forgetfulness and introduces an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Understanding this nuance is crucial for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the rule and its basis
Identify the ruling: Witr cannot precede Isha due to the necessary order. The basis is the hadith 'Make Witr the last of your night prayers' and the Prophet's practice.
The command 'اجعلوا' indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the implied question
The text answers an implied question: why can't Witr be prayed before its time has entered? Because of the order, not because the time is invalid.
Witr's time begins after Isha, but even after its time starts, precedence is forbidden.
3
Distinguish the exception for forgetfulness
According to Abu Hanifa, if one forgets and prays Witr before Isha, Witr is valid and not repeated. This is the mufta bihi view.
The text says 'لا يعيد الوتر' (he does not repeat Witr).
4
Analyze the disagreement with the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that Witr must be repeated if forgotten, because Witr is a follower (taba') of Isha and order is essential.
The text states 'عندهما يعيد'.
5
Apply the ruling to the given example
Work through the example: someone prays Isha without wudu, then sleeps, makes wudu, prays Witr, then remembers. According to Abu Hanifa, only Isha is repeated; Witr is valid.
This illustrates the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يقدم الوتر على العشاء للترتيب اللازم. أطلقه وهو مقيد بالتذكر كما هو مذكور في "البداية"، فلو قدم الوتر على العشاء ناسيا لا يعيد الوتر، وكذا لو صلى العشاء بغير طهارة ثم نام فقام وتوضأ وصلى الوتر، ثم تذكر أنه صلى العشاء بغير طهارة، يعيدها دون الوتر فيهما. للترتيب اللازم أي لا يقدم الوتر على العشاء؛ لوجوب الترتيب اللازم بين العشاء والوتر، وهذا جواب عن سؤال مقدر تقريره لم لا يجوز تقديمه بعد دخول وقته؟ أجاب بأنه إنما لا يجوز؛ للترتيب، لا لكون الوقت لم يدخل، وهذا على قوله، وعلى قولهما؛ لأنه تبع للعشاء، وأثر الخلاف يظهر فيما لو قدم الوتر عليها ناسياً أو تذكر أنه صلاها فقط على غير وضوء لا يعيده عنده وعندهما يعيد. ومن لم يجد إلخ أي من لم يجد وقت العشاء والوتر بأن كان في بلد يطلع الفجر كما تغرب الشمس، أو قبل أن يغيب الشفق لم يجبا عليه؛ لعدم السبب، وهو الوقت.
He should not precede Witr before Isha due to the necessary order. This is unrestricted but is restricted by the qualification of remembering, as mentioned in al-Bidaya. So if one precedes Witr before Isha out of forgetfulness, he does not repeat Witr. Similarly, if he prayed Isha without purification, then slept, got up, performed ablution, and prayed Witr, then remembered that he had prayed Isha without purification, he repeats Isha but not Witr in both cases. For the necessary order, i.e., he should not precede Witr before Isha because of the obligation of the necessary order between Isha and Witr. This is an answer to an implied question: 'Why is it not permissible to present it after its time has entered?' He answered: 'It is not permissible due to order, not because the time has not entered.' This is according to his view (Abu Hanifa) and according to their view (the two Sahibayn) because it is a follower of Isha. The effect of the difference appears in the case where one presents it (Witr) before it (Isha) forgetfully, or remembers that he performed Isha only but without ablution: he does not repeat it (Witr) according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to them he repeats. And whoever does not find, etc.: i.e., whoever does not find the time of Isha and Witr, such as if he is in a land where dawn appears as the sun sets, or before the twilight disappears, they are not obligatory for him due to the absence of the cause, which is time.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First: It is obligatory that Witr be prayed after Isha due to the necessary order (tartib lazim) between them. One cannot pray Witr before Isha. However, this ruling is qualified: if one forgets and prays Witr before Isha, he does not repeat Witr according to Abu Hanifa. An example is given: if someone prays Isha without wudu, then sleeps, wakes up, makes wudu, prays Witr, and then remembers the Isha was invalid, he repeats only Isha, not Witr. The reason for the order is that Witr is 'taba'' (follower) of Isha. If one intentionally prays Witr before Isha, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. Second: The ruling on those who do not experience the time of Isha and Witr (e.g., in polar regions where dawn appears immediately after sunset or before shafaq disappears) – for such people, the prayers are not obligatory because the cause (sabab) of obligation, which is the time, is absent.

Key Terms
الترتيب اللازم (al-tartib al-lazim): The necessary sequential order that must be observed between Isha and Witr; Witr cannot be prayed before Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person prays Witr before Isha out of forgetfulness, according to Abu Hanifa, what must he do?
A) Repeat Witr after Isha
B) Repeat both Isha and Witr
C) Repeat only Isha, Witr is valid
D) Nothing, it is valid as is

Key Takeaway
The order between Isha and Witr is wajib; only forgetfulness (according to Abu Hanifa) excuses the precedence without requiring repetition.

Defining Shafaq: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Twilight
Defines shafaq and presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on its interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conflicting definitions of shafaq within the Hanafi school, explain the preferred view (mufta bihi), and apply the ruling to determine the times of Maghrib and Isha.

Core Idea
The ultimate Hanafi position is that shafaq is the redness; the earlier view of whiteness is no longer operative.

In determining the prayer times, the definition of shafaq (twilight) is crucial. This passage from Nur al-Idah not only states the relied-upon view but also preserves a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. Understanding this dispute helps us see how later Hanafi scholars settled the issue, ensuring we pray at the correct times.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed-upon end of Maghrib time
All scholars agree that Maghrib time ends at the disappearance of shafaq. Identify this common ground from the passage.
2
Identify the two definitions of shafaq
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and later Abu Hanifa, shafaq is the redness (humra). According to Abu Hanifa's original view, shafaq is the whiteness (bayad) after redness. Note both definitions from the text.
3
Understand the primary difference in timing
The difference in definition affects the length of Maghrib time: redness ends earlier (about 30-45 min after sunset), whiteness ends later (up to 1.5 hours). Calculate the practical impact.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's retraction and the later tarjih
The passage mentions that Abu Hanifa returned to the redness view. Later scholars, as in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, preferred the Imam's view (i.e., his final view). Recognize that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the redness.
5
Apply the mufta bihi definition to find Isha time
Isha begins at the disappearance of shafaq according to the chosen definition. Using the redness view, a person should pray Isha after the redness vanishes. Confirm with the passage's statement about consensus (ijma' al-salaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمغرب منه إلى غروب الشفق الأحمر على المفتى به والعشاء والوتر منه إلى الصبح الصادق إجماعاً. الشفق: اعلم أنهم اتفقوا على أن منتهى وقت المغرب إلى الشفق، ولكن اختلفوا في تفسير الشفق، فقالا: الشفق الحمرة، وإليه يروى رجوع أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو حنيفة: الشفق هو البياض الذي بعد الحمرة، فوقت المغرب أزيد عند أبي حنيفة منه عندهما، ورجح في البحر قول الإمام والعشاء: أي ابتداء وقت صلاة العشاء والوتر من غروب الشفق على الاختلاف الذي تقدم إلى قبيل طلوع الصبح الصادق؛ لإجماع السلف.
And Maghrib (extends) from it to the disappearance of the red twilight according to the relied-upon view, and Isha and Witr from it to the true dawn by consensus. The twilight: Know that they agreed that the end of Maghrib time is the twilight, but they differed in its interpretation. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the twilight is the redness, and it is narrated that Abu Hanifa returned to this view. Abu Hanifa said: the twilight is the whiteness that follows the redness, so Maghrib time is longer according to Abu Hanifa than according to them. In al-Bahr, Imam's view was preferred. And Isha: i.e., the beginning of the time for Isha and Witr is from the disappearance of the twilight, according to the difference mentioned, to just before the true dawn, due to consensus of the predecessors.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage begins with a ruling statement from the matn: Maghrib time lasts from its entry (after the setting of the sun) until the disappearance of the red twilight (shafaq al-ahmar), according to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi). Then it states that the time of Isha and Witr is from the disappearance of the shafaq until the break of true dawn (subh sadiq) by consensus. The commentary then opens a discussion on the definition of 'shafaq'. It notes that all scholars agree that the end of Maghrib time is shafaq, but they differ in interpreting it. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), shafaq is the redness (humra). It is also narrated that Abu Hanifa retracted his original view and adopted this interpretation. In the earlier view of Abu Hanifa, shafaq is the whiteness (bayad) that appears after the redness. Consequently, Maghrib time is longer according to Abu Hanifa's original position than according to the Sahibayn. The commentator mentions that in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the view of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is preferred. Then the passage returns to the ruling: the beginning of Isha and Witr time is from the disappearance of shafaq, according to whichever interpretation, extending until just before true dawn, based on the consensus of the early generations (ijma' al-salaf). Thus, the definition of shafaq directly affects both the end of Maghrib and the start of Isha.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, it is the redness (al-humra), and according to an earlier Hanafi view, it is the whiteness (al-bayad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what does 'shafaq' refer to?
A) The redness after sunset
B) The whiteness after redness
C) Both equally valid
D) The total darkness

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view defines shafaq as the redness; thus Maghrib ends and Isha begins with the disappearance of redness.

Combining Prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah: Conditions and Ruling
Ruling on combining prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two places where combining prayers is permitted in the Hanafi school and identify the specific conditions (Imam al-A'zam, ihram) required for validity.

Core Idea
Combining prayers is only allowed at Arafat and Muzdalifah during Hajj, with strict conditions.

Normally, the Hanafi school prohibits combining two obligatory prayers in one time without a valid excuse. However, during Hajj, a dispensation allows combining at two specific locations: Arafat and Muzdalifah. This lesson explains the conditions—being with the Supreme Imam and in the state of ihram—and how the prayers are combined at each place.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The text begins with 'ولا يجمع بين فرضين في وقت بعذر إلا في عرفة للحاج' stating that combining is not allowed except at Arafat. This establishes the exceptional nature.
2
Examine the conditions for Arafat
The conditions are 'بشرط الإمام الأعظم والإحرام' — the presence of the supreme Imam (or his deputy) and being in ihram for Hajj.
3
Understand the combination at Arafat
At Arafat, Dhuhr and Asr are combined in advance (jamm' taqdim) with one adhan and two iqamas.
4
Understand the combination at Muzdalifah
At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are combined (jamm' ta'khir) with one adhan and one iqama. Maghrib cannot be prayed on the way to Muzdalifah.
5
Note the key distinctions
The text details the different procedures at the two places, including the number of adhan and iqama.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين فرضين في وقت بعذر إلا في عرفة للحاج بشرط الإمام الأعظم والإحرام، فيجمع بين الظهر والعصر جمع تقديم، ويجمع بين المغرب والعشاء بمزدلفة. هو في وقت الظهر. ولم تجز المغرب في طريق مزدلفة، ويجمع إلخ بأذان واحد وإقامتين. ويجمع إلخ بأذان واحد وإقامة واحدة.
And he should not combine two obligatory prayers in one time due to an excuse except at Arafah for the pilgrim, on condition of the greatest Imam and ihram. So he combines Dhuhr and Asr as an advance combination, and he combines Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. That is in the time of Dhuhr. And Maghrib is not permissible on the way to Muzdalifah. And he combines etc. with one adhan and two iqamas. And he combines etc. with one adhan and one iqama.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage outlines the exceptional dispensation of combining (jamm') two obligatory prayers in one time, which is normally prohibited. The only allowed instances are: (1) At Arafat during Hajj: the pilgrim combines Dhuhr and Asr by advancing Asr to the time of Dhuhr (jamm' taqdim). (2) At Muzdalifah: the pilgrim combines Maghrib and Isha by delaying Maghrib to the time of Isha (jamm' ta'khir). Conditions for the validity at Arafat include: the presence of the 'Imam al-A'zam' (the supreme ruler or his deputy) leading the prayer, and the pilgrim must be in the state of ihram for Hajj (not for Umrah). The Maghrib prayer must not be performed on the way to Muzdalifah; it must be delayed until reaching Muzdalifah. The text also notes that at Arafat, the combination is done with one adhan and two iqamas, while at Muzdalifah, it is with one adhan and one iqama. The conditions are tight to ensure this dispensation is limited to the specific Hajj context.

Key Terms
جمع التقديم (jamm' al-taqdim): To pray the second prayer in the time of the first (e.g., Asr in Dhuhr time) at Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where is combining (jamm') between Maghrib and Isha permitted in the Hanafi school?
A) At any travel destination
B) At Arafat only
C) At Muzdalifah only
D) At both Arafat and Muzdalifah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits combining prayers only at Arafat (Dhuhr and Asr) and Muzdalifah (Maghrib and Isha) during Hajj, subject to the conditions of being with the Imam and in ihram.

Recommended Times for Prayers (Mustahabbat)
Lists preferred times for each prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) timing for each of the five daily prayers and identify the exceptions for cloudy days.

Core Idea
Pray at the preferred time: Fajr in brightness, Zuhr cool in summer, Asr before the sun changes, Maghrib early, Isha delayed, Witr at night's end.

This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the mustahabb (recommended) timings for each of the five obligatory prayers and Witr. While the prayer is valid throughout its entire time window, performing it at the preferred time brings greater reward. The rulings consider seasonal variations and weather conditions, especially cloudy days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer and the general rule
For each prayer, note whether the recommended action is ta'jil (hasten) or ta'khir (delay). For example, Fajr is delayed (isfar) for men, Zuhr is delayed in summer (ibrad) and hastened in winter, Asr is delayed, Maghrib is hastened, Isha is delayed, Witr is delayed.
General rules apply to clear weather conditions.
2
Note the exception for cloudy days
Cloudy days flip some rules: For Zuhr, delay even in winter; for Asr, hasten instead of delay; for Maghrib, delay instead of hasten; for Isha, hasten instead of delay. Fajr and Witr have no cloudy day exception mentioned.
The underlying wisdom is that cloudy skies make it harder to determine the exact time.
3
Understand the rationale for each timing
Isfar (brightness) for Fajr helps men ensure they have prayed within the proper time. Ibrad (cooling) for Zuhr in summer avoids praying in extreme heat. Delaying Asr until before the sun changes (yellowing) is best. Hastening Maghrib ensures it is performed soon after sunset. Delaying Isha to one-third of the night allows people to rest. Delaying Witr to the last part of the night is for those confident of waking.
These preferences are based on ease and optimal conditions for devotion.
4
Apply to women's rulings
Women are encouraged to pray Fajr earlier in darkness for concealment, and similar considerations apply to other prayers where darkness provides modesty.
This is a madhhab-specific nuance not explicitly in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب الإسفار بالفجر للرجال والإبراد بالظهر وهو التأخير للإضاءة في الصيف، وتعجيله في الشتاء إلا في يوم غيم، فيؤخر فيه، وتأخير العصر ما لم تتغير الشمس صيفاً وشتاءً، وتعجيله في يوم الغيم، وتعجيل المغرب إلا في يوم غيم، فيؤخر فيه، وتأخير العشاء إلى ثلث الليل، وتعجيله في الغيم، وتأخير الوتر إلى آخر الليل لمن يثق بالانتباه.
And it is recommended to make the Fajr prayer bright for men, and to make the Zuhr prayer cool, which means delaying for clarity in summer, and hastening it in winter except on a cloudy day, then delay it. And delaying the Asr prayer as long as the sun has not changed, summer and winter, and hastening it on a cloudy day. And hastening the Maghrib prayer except on a cloudy day, then delay it. And delaying the Isha prayer until a third of the night, and hastening it in cloudiness. And delaying the Witr prayer until the end of the night for one who is confident of waking.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage enumerates the recommended (mustahabb) timings for each of the five daily prayers (Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha) and Witr. For Fajr, it is recommended for men to delay until there is enough light (isfar) rather than praying in deep darkness. For Zuhr, in summer it is recommended to delay (ibrad) until it is cooler, and in winter to pray early, except on cloudy days where it is better to delay. For Asr, it is recommended to delay as long as the sun has not changed colour (turned yellow), summer and winter; on cloudy days, hasten it. For Maghrib, it is recommended to pray it immediately (ta'jil), except on cloudy days when it is better to delay a bit. For Isha, it is recommended to delay until about one-third of the night, and to hasten on cloudy nights. For Witr, it is recommended to delay until the end of the night if one is confident of waking up; otherwise, it should be prayed before sleep. These rulings apply to men specifically in some cases; women have different considerations (e.g., concealing themselves in darkness).

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isar): To delay Fajr prayer until there is sufficient light (brightness) in the sky, which is recommended for men.
الإبراد (al-ibrad): To delay Zuhr prayer in summer until the intensity of heat subsides, making it cooler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pray it immediately as usual
B) Delay it a bit
C) Combine with Isha
D) Pray it earlier than usual

Key Takeaway
Observing the recommended timings increases reward, and exceptions for cloudy days show the flexibility of Islamic law.
