Responding to the Adhan and Supplication
Response to the adhan and supplication after it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for responding to each part of the adhan and apply them when hearing the adhan.

Core Idea
Do not repeat 'hayya 'ala al-salah'; say 'la hawla'; for 'al-salahu khayrun', say 'sadaqta'.

When the mu'adhdhin calls to prayer, the listener is encouraged to respond. However, the Hanafi school prescribes specific responses for certain phrases to avoid mockery and to acknowledge one's dependence on Allah. This lesson covers the proper response to each part of the adhan and the recommended supplication after it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main components of the adhan
Recall the phrases of the adhan: Allahu Akbar, Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah, Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah, and in Fajr, 'Al-salahu khayrun min al-nawm'.
2
Determine the response for each phrase
For most phrases, you repeat exactly what the mu'adhdhin says, except for the hay'alahs (Hayya 'ala al-salah and Hayya 'ala al-falah) and the Fajr phrase.
3
Apply the special responses for hay'alah and Fajr
For the hay'alahs, say 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (there is no power and no strength except with Allah). For 'Al-salahu khayrun min al-nawm', say 'Sadaqta wa bararta' or 'Ma sha' Allah'.
This avoids the appearance of commanding oneself.
4
After the adhan, make the supplication for wasilah
Both the mu'adhdhin and the listener should supplicate: 'Allahumma rabba hadhihi al-da'wati al-tammati wa al-salati al-qa'imati, ati Muhammadan al-wasilata wa al-fadilata wab'athhu maqaman mahmudan alladhi wa'adtahu'. Avoid additions like 'al-darajata al-rafi'ah' which are not authentically reported.
5
Review the sunnah nature of responding
Responding to the adhan is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). It is not obligatory but highly recommended.
The Hanafi position is clear: the response is sunnah, and these specific phrases are part of that sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا سمع المسنون منه أمسك، وقال مثله، وحوقل في الحيعلتين . صبي كان ممن يعقل أيضاً. ما لا لحن فيه الجمعة وصبي: أي يكره بل لا . أذان يصح غير عاقل، وقيد بكونه ممن لا يعقل فأفاد أنه إن كان ممن يعقل لا يكره أذانه، وقيل: يكره أذانه، وإن ويستحب إلخ أي إذا تكلم المؤذن في أثناء الصلاة أو في أثناء الإقامة يستحب أن يعاد الأذان لا الإقامة ويكرهان أي إذا لم يدرك الجمعة جماعة، فأرادت أداءها بالجماعة في المصر كره لهم الأذان والإقامة كجماعتهم قيد بـ'المصر'؛ لأن أهل السواد لا يكره لهم أداء ظهر يوم بالأذان والإقامة؛ لأنه لا جمعة عليهم. ويؤذن للفائتة أطلقه فشمل ما إذا قضاها في بيته أو في المسجد، وفي 'المجتبى' معزيا إلى الحلواني: 'أنه سنة القضاء في البيوت دون المساجد، فإن فيه تشويشا وتغليطا ، وإذا كانوا قد صرحوا بأن الفائتة لا تقضى في المسجد؛ لما فيه من إظهار التكاسل في إخراج الصلاة عن وقتها، فالواجب الإخفاء، فالأذان للفائتة أولى بالمنع. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٩/١] وكذا لأولى الفوائت: أي إن فاتته صلوات أذن للأولى وأقام، وفي البواقي مخيرٌ إن شاء أذن وأقام، وإن شاء اقتصر على الإقامة، هذا إذا قضاها في مجلس واحد، أما إذا قضاها في مجالس، فيشترط كلاهما. وإذا سمع إلخ : أفاد أنه لو لم يسمع لبعد أو صمم لا يشرع له الإمساك، ولو علم أنه أذان، وقيد بالمسنون من الأذان، فأفاد أنه إذا كان على غير وجه السنة كأذان المرأة وغيره لا تندب له المتابعة فقوله: 'أمسك' أي امتنع عن كل شيء يخل بالاستماع والإجابة حتى عن التلاوة؛ ليجيب المؤذن، وفي وجوب إجابة الأذان وندبها كلام يطلب من المطولات وحوقل أي يقول: 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله' إذا قال المؤذن: 'حي على الصلاة'، 'حي على الفلاح'، والسر في اختصاصهما بذلك أنه لما طلب منهم الإقبال على الصلاة والمجيء إليها وطلب منهم بقوله: 'حي على الفلاح' الإقبال إلى الفوز والنجاة، وذلك لا يكون إلا بحركة والعبد لا قدرة له على شيء، ناسب أن يقول: لا حول أي لا حركة ولا استطاعة لي على شيء مما طلب مني إلا بقوة الله تعالى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٣] ولو قال مثل ما قال المؤذن لكان كالمستهزئ؛ لأن من حكى لفظ الأمر بشيء كان مستهزئاً به بخلاف باقي الكلمات؛ لأنه ثناء، والدعاء مستجاب بعد إجابته بمثل ما قال. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٠٤] وقال: صدقت وبررت، أو 'ما شاء الله' عند قول المؤذن: 'الصلاة خير من النوم'، ثم دعا بالوسيلة فيقول: اللهم رب هذه الدعوة التامة، والصلاة القائمة، آت محمدا الوسيلة والفضيلة وابعثه مقاما محمودا الذي وعدته. وقال صدقت إلخ: أي وفي أذان الفجر قال الذي يجيب أذان المؤذن: صدقت وبررت، أو يقول: 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' عند قول المؤذن: 'الصلاة خير من النوم'؛ تحاشيا عما يشبه الاستهزاء. دعا بالوسيلة : أي كل واحد من المؤذن والمجيب [الزيلعي بتصرف] الوسيلة: هي فعيلة، وتجمع على وسائل ووسل، وهي كل أمر يكون موصلا لأمر تبتغيه، وحقيقة الوسيلة إلى الله عز وجل مراعاة سبيله بالعلم والعبادة، وتحري مكارم الشريعة فهي كالقربة قاله الراغب وحاصله أنها فعل المأمورات واجتناب المنهيات، والمراد هنا منزلة عالية في الجنة، فهو مجاز من إطلاق السبب على المسبب . [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٤] والفضيلة: هي المرتبة الزائدة على سائر الخلق أو منزلة أخرى، أو تفسير للوسيلة. قال السخاوي في 'المقاصد الحسنة': وزيادة 'الدرجة الرفيعة' كما يفعله من لا خبرة له بالسنة لا أصل لها في الدعاء الوارد ذكره الشهاب في شرح الشفاء'. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٥]
And if one hears the sunnah [adhan] from him, he should refrain [from speech] and say the like [of what the mu'adhdhin says], and he should say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' during the two hay'alahs. [Commentary continues with explanations of various points, including the ruling on the adhan of a boy, the dislike of adhan and iqamah for Friday, making up missed prayers, the response to the adhan, and the supplication after the adhan.] And he said: 'Sadaqta wa bararta' or 'Ma sha' Allah' at the mu'adhdhin's saying 'al-salahu khayrun min al-nawm', then he supplicates for al-wasilah saying: 'Allahumma rabba hadhihi al-da'wati al-tammati wa al-salati al-qa'imati, ati Muhammadan al-wasilata wa al-fadilata wab'athhu maqaman mahmudan alladhi wa'adtahu.' And he said: 'Sadaqta' etc.: that is, in the adhan of Fajr, the responder says: 'Sadaqta wa bararta' or 'Ma sha' Allah kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun' at the mu'adhdhin's saying 'al-salahu khayrun min al-nawm', avoiding what resembles mockery. He supplicates for al-wasilah: that is, each one of the mu'adhdhin and the responder [the explanation of wasilah and fadilah follows].
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage details the proper response to the adhan. It begins by stating that upon hearing the adhan (that is sunnah), one should stop speaking and repeat the phrases after the mu'adhdhin, except for the two hay'alahs ('hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah'), where one should say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (there is no power and no strength except with Allah). The commentary explains that this is because these phrases are a call to action, and a person acknowledges his inability without divine aid. Responding with the exact words would be like mocking, as it would seem to command oneself. For the phrase 'al-salahu khayrun min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep) in the Fajr adhan, one says 'sadaqta wa bararta' (you have spoken truth and done well) or 'ma sha' Allah' (whatever Allah wills). Then, after the adhan, both the mu'adhdhin and the listener should supplicate for al-wasilah (the means) for the Prophet ﷺ using the well-known du'a: 'Allahumma rabba hadhihi al-da'wati...' The commentary clarifies that al-wasilah is a high station in Paradise, and al-fadilah is an additional rank. It warns against adding 'al-darajata al-rafi'ah' which has no basis in the sunnah. The passage also revisits earlier rulings on adhan by a child, missed prayers, and the dislike of adhan and iqamah in certain contexts, integrating them into the discussion of response.

Key Terms
الحيعلة (al-hay'alah): The phrase 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah' in the adhan.
الوسيلة (al-wasilah): A high station in Paradise that will be granted to the Prophet ﷺ.
الصلاة خير من النوم (al-salahu khayrun min al-nawm): A phrase added in the Fajr adhan meaning 'prayer is better than sleep'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person say when the mu'adhdhin says 'hayya 'ala al-salah'?
A) 'Hayya 'ala al-salah'
B) 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'
C) 'Sadaqta wa bararta'
D) 'Allahu akbar'

Key Takeaway
When hearing the adhan, follow the Hanafi sunnah: repeat most phrases, but say 'la hawla' for hay'alah and 'sadaqta' for the Fajr phrase, then supplicate for wasilah.

Responding to the Adhan: The Phrase 'Al-Salatu Khayrun min al-Nawm' and the Supplication for Wasilah
Ruling statement on recommended responses to Fajr adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended responses to the Fajr adhan phrase 'Al-Salatu Khayrun min al-Nawm' and identify the correct supplication for Wasilah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
When hearing 'الصلاة خير من النوم', respond with 'صدقت وبررت' — not repetition — to avoid mockery, then ask for Wasilah.

In the Fajr adhan, the mu'adhdhin calls out 'الصلاة خير من النوم' (Prayer is better than sleep). How should we respond? This lesson explains the Hanafi sunnah response, why repeating the phrase is discouraged, and the blessed supplication for the Prophet's high station. Understanding this completes the etiquette of answering the call to prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special phrase in Fajr adhan
Recognize that 'الصلاة خير من النوم' is only said in the Fajr adhan. This phrase requires a distinct response.
It is not said in other prayers.
2
Recall the recommended responses
The text gives two options: 'صدقت وبررت' (You have spoken the truth and acted righteously) or 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' (Whatever Allah wills was and whatever He does not will was not).
Either is acceptable, but 'صدقت وبررت' is more common.
3
Understand the reason for not repeating
Repeating the phrase could resemble mockery (استهزاء), so the sunnah provides a different response.
The text says 'تحاشيا عما يشبه الاستهزاء'.
4
Learn the du'a for Wasilah
After the adhan, one should say: 'اللهم رب هذه الدعوة التامة، والصلاة القائمة، آت محمدا الوسيلة والفضيلة وابعثه مقاما محمودا الذي وعدته.'
This du'a is recommended for both the mu'adhdhin and the listener.
5
Note the prohibition of additions
The hashiyah warns against adding 'الدرجة الرفيعة' to the du'a, as it has no basis in the Sunnah.
Al-Sakhawi confirms this in al-Maqasid al-Hasanah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة ۷۳ حكم الأذان والإقامة وقال: صدقت وبررت"، أو "ما شاء الله عند قول المؤذن: "الصلاة خير من النوم"، ثم دعا بالوسيلة فيقول: اللهم رب هذه الدعوة التامة، والصلاة القائمة، آت محمدا الوسيلة والفضيلة وابعثه مقاما محمودا الذي وعدته. وقال صدقت إلخ: أي وفي أذان الفجر قال الذي يجيب أذان المؤذن: صدقت وبررت"، أو يقول: "ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن عند قول المؤذن: "الصلاة" خير من النوم؛ تحاشيا عما يشبه الاستهزاء. دعا بالوسيلة : أي كل واحد من المؤذن والمجيب الزيلعي بتصرف) الوسيلة: هي فعيلة، وتجمع على وسائل ووسل، وهي كل أمر يكون موصلا لأمر تبتغيه، وحقيقة الوسيلة إلى الله عز وجل مراعاة سبيله بالعلم والعبادة، وتحري مكارم الشريعة فهي كالقربة قاله الراغب وحاصله أنها فعل المأمورات واجتناب المنهيات، والمراد هنا منزلة عالية في الجنة، فهو مجاز من إطلاق السبب على المسبب . [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٤] والفضيلة: هي المرتبة الزائدة على سائر الخلق أو منزلة أخرى، أو تفسير للوسيلة. قال السخاوي في "المقاصد الحسنة": وزيادة "الدرجة الرفيعة" كما يفعله من لا خبرة له بالسنة لا أصل لها في الدعاء الوارد ذكره الشهاب في شرح الشفاء". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٥]
The ruling of the adhan and iqamah. And he said: 'You have spoken the truth and acted righteously' or 'Whatever Allah wills' at the saying of the mu'adhdhin: 'Prayer is better than sleep', then he asks for al-wasilah saying: 'O Allah, Lord of this perfect call and the established prayer, grant Muhammad the wasilah and the excellence, and raise him to a praiseworthy station which You have promised him.' And he said 'You have spoken the truth' etc.: That is, in the Fajr adhan, the one who responds to the adhan says: 'You have spoken the truth and acted righteously' or he says: 'Whatever Allah wills was, and whatever He does not will was not' at the saying of the mu'adhdhin: 'Prayer is better than sleep,' avoiding what resembles mockery. He asks for al-wasilah: i.e., each one of the mu'adhdhin and the respondent (al-Zayla'i with modification). Al-wasilah: it is on the pattern of fa'ilah, and its plural is wasa'il and wasl, and it is every matter that leads to a sought-after matter. The reality of wasilah to Allah Almighty is to observe His path through knowledge and worship, and to pursue the noble traits of the Shariah, so it is like a means of nearness, as al-Raghib said. Its summary is that it is doing what is commanded and avoiding what is prohibited. What is meant here is a high station in Paradise, so it is a metaphor of applying the cause to the effect. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 204] And al-fadilah: is the additional rank over all creation or another station, or an explanation of wasilah. al-Sakhawi in 'al-Maqasid al-Hasanah' said: The addition of 'al-darajah al-rafi'ah' as done by those who have no knowledge of the Sunnah has no basis in the reported supplication, as mentioned by al-Shihab in 'Sharh al-Shifa'. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 205]
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah explains the etiquettes of responding to the adhan, specifically during the Fajr adhan when the mu'adhdhin says "الصلاة خير من النوم" (Prayer is better than sleep). The responder is recommended to say either "صدقت وبررت" (You have spoken the truth and acted righteously) or "ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن" (Whatever Allah wills was, and whatever He does not will was not). The author notes that this is done to avoid any semblance of mockery, as repeating the phrase could be misconstrued. After the adhan, the responder should then supplicate with the well-known du'a asking Allah to grant the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) al-wasilah (a high station in Paradise) and al-fadilah (excellence). The commentary elaborates on the meaning of wasilah, explaining that it is a means of nearness to Allah through knowledge and worship, and here it refers to the highest rank in Paradise. The hashiyah adds that the addition of "الدرجة الرفيعة" (the high degree) in the du'a has no basis in the Sunnah, as noted by al-Sakhawi. This is a ruling stating the recommended (mustahab) actions for one who hears the adhan, without explicit proof, but it is based on established practice.

Key Terms
الوسيلة (al-wasilah): A high station in Paradise that is promised to the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) and is asked for in the du'a after the adhan. In general, it means a means of nearness to Allah.
الفضيلة (al-fadilah): Excellence or additional rank over all creation, or another station in Paradise. Some commentators explain it as a synonym for al-wasilah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the mu'adhdhin says 'الصلاة خير من النوم' in the Fajr adhan, what is the recommended response according to the Hanafi school?
A) Repeat the same phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم'
B) Say 'صدقت وبررت' or 'ما شاء الله كان'
C) Remain silent until the du'a
D) Say 'لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله'

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to respond to 'الصلاة خير من النوم' with 'صدقت وبررت' and to ask for al-wasilah without additions.

Defining Shart and Rukn: The Framework for Prayer Validity
Defines shart and rukn, classifies shurut into four types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of shart and rukn and classify the four types of shurut (shart al-in'iqaad, shart al-in'iqaad wa al-dawam, shart al-baqa', shart al-khuruj) with examples.

Core Idea
A shart is external, a rukn is integral; conditions for prayer are of four types based on when they apply.

Understanding the precise meaning of shart (condition) and rukn (pillar) is foundational to mastering the fiqh of prayer. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definitions and provides a four-part classification of conditions (shurut) that govern the validity and continuity of prayer. By parsing these distinctions, you will gain clarity on what is required at each stage of performing salat.

Guided Path
1
Define shart and rukn
Read the definitions from the text: shart is something external whose existence is necessary; rukn is an integral part of the essence. Note the linguistic and technical meanings.
Shart is broader than rukn in conditionality.
2
Identify the three general types of shart
The text mentions three types: rational ('aqli), legal (shar'i), and stipulative (ja'li). Give an example of each.
Only the legal type concerns us in fiqh.
3
Learn the four specific shurut for prayer
The commentary classifies conditions for prayer into four: for validity only, for validity and continuity, for continuity only, and for exiting. List each with an example from the text.
Shart al-baqa' is subdivided into existential and non-existential.
4
Distinguish the role of shart vs rukn
Understand that a condition (shart) is external, while a pillar (rukn) is internal. A missing rukn invalidates the act entirely; a missing condition prevents initiation or continuation.
This classification is unique to Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة ٧٤ شروط الصلاة وأركانها باب شروط الصلاة وأركانها لابد لصحة الصلاة من سبعة وعشرين شيئا : الطهارة من الحدث، وطهارة الجسد، الأصغر والأكبر والثوب والمكان من نجس غير معفو عنه حتى موضع القدمين، واليدين، والركبتين، كما قدمناه والجبهة على الأصح ، وستر العورة، ولا يضر نظرها من جيبه. إجماعا لكنه خلاف الأدب شروط جمع شرط بسكون الراء، وهو ثلاثة أنواع: عقلي كالقدوم للنجار، وشرعي كالطهارة للصلاة، وجعلي كالدخول المعلق به الطلاق. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٦] وهو في الشريعة: ما يتوقف على وجوده الشيء، وهو خارج عن ماهيته. والأركان جمع ركن وهو في اللغة الجانب الأقوى، وفي الاصطلاح: الجزء الذي تتركب الماهية منه ومن غيره. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٠٦] اعلم ان الشروط من حيث هي أربعة أقسام: (۱) شرط انعقاد لا غير ،كالنية والتحريمة والوقت، والخطبة للجمعة. (۲) وشرط انعقاد ودوام كالطهارة، وستر العورة، واستقبال القبلة. (۳) وشرط بقاء لا غير أي ما يشترط وجوده داخل الصلاة، وهو نوعان أيضا وجودي وعدمي، فالوجودي كالقراءة، فإنها وإن كانت ركنا إلا أنها ركن في نفسها شرط لغيرها؛ لوجودها في كل الأركان تقديرا، ولذا لم يجز استخلاف الأمي ولو بعد أداء فرض القراءة كما في "الدر"، والعدمي كعدم تقدم المقتدي على إمامه وعدم محاذاة مشتهاة في صلاة مشتركة، وعدم تذكر صاحب الترتيب فائتة. (٤) والقسم الرابع: شرط خروج، وهو القعدة الأخيرة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٧] وعشرين: لا حصر فيها، ومن اقتصر على ذكر الشروط الستة الخارجة عن الصلاة، وعلى الستة الأركان الداخلة فيها أراد التقريب، وإلا فالمصلي يحتاج إلى ما ذكرناه بزيادة فأردنا به بيان ما إليه الحاجة من شرط صحة الشروع والدوام على صحتها، وكلها ،فروض وعبر بلفظ الشيء الصادق بالشرط والركن [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٠٧] والمكان أي موضع قدميه أو إحداهما إن رفع الأخرى. [الدر المختار: ٤٠٣/١] سبعة واليدين: أي ومن الشروط طهارة موضع اليدين والركبتين على الصحيح واختاره الفقيه أبو الليث، وأنكر ما قيل من عدم افتراض طهارة موضعها مراقي الفلاح (۲۰۹] على الأصح وفي رواية عن الإمام لا يشترط طهارة موضع السجود، أي بناء على رواية جواز الاقتصار على الأنف في السجود، فلا يشترط طهارة موضع الأنف؛ لأنه أقل من الدرهم. رد المحتار: ٤٠٣/١] وستر العورة: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان بحضرته أحد أو لم يكن، حتى لو صلى في بيت مظلم عرياناً وله ثوب طاهر لا يجوز إجماعاً؛ لأن الستر مشتمل على حق الله وحق العباد، وإن كان مراعى في الجملة بسبب استتاره عنهم فحق الله تعالى ليس كذلك، فإن قيل: الستر لا يجب عن الله تعالى؛ لأنه سبحانه يرى المستور كما يرى المكشوف. أجيب بأنه يرى المكشوف تاركًا للأدب والمستور متأدباً، وهذا الأدب واجب مراعاة عند القدرة عليه. [البحر الرائق: ٥٣٠/١]
Chapter of the conditions of prayer and its pillars. For the validity of prayer, twenty-seven things are necessary: purification from hadath (ritual impurity), purification of the body (minor and major), and of the garment and place from impurity that is not excusable, even the place of the feet, the hands, the knees, as we have mentioned, and the forehead on the most correct view, and covering the nakedness (awrah), and it does not harm if she sees it from her collar, by consensus, but it is contrary to good manners. Conditions (shurut) is the plural of shart with sukun on the ra, and it is of three types: rational, like the arrival for the carpenter; legal, like purification for prayer; and stipulative, like the entry on which divorce is conditioned. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 206] And it (shart) in the Shariah is: that upon whose existence something depends, and it is external to its essence. And arkan (pillars) is the plural of rukn, which in language means the strongest side, and in terminology: the part from which the essence is composed and from others. [Maraqi al-Falah: 206] Know that conditions are four types: (1) A condition for validity only (shart in'iqaad), like intention, takbirat al-ihram, time, and the sermon for Friday prayer. (2) A condition for validity and continuity, like purification, covering the awrah, and facing the qibla. (3) A condition for continuity only (shart baqa'), i.e., what must exist inside the prayer, and it is of two types: existential and non-existential. The existential is like recitation, for although it is a pillar, it is a pillar in itself and a condition for others, because it exists in all pillars virtually, and therefore it is not permissible to appoint an illiterate person as imam even after performing the obligation of recitation, as in al-Durr. The non-existential is like that the follower does not precede the imam, and that there is no alignment of a desire in a shared prayer, and that the one with a missed prayer sequence does not remember a missed prayer. (4) The fourth type: a condition for exiting (shart khuruj), which is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah). [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 207] And 'twenty': there is no limit to it, and whoever restricts himself to mentioning the six conditions external to prayer and the six pillars internal to it intended simplification, otherwise the worshiper needs what we have mentioned with addition, so we wanted to show what is needed of conditions for valid commencement and continuity in its validity, and all of them are obligations (furud). And he expressed with the word 'thing' which applies to both condition and pillar. [Maraqi al-Falah: 207] And 'the place' means the place of his feet or one of them if he lifts the other. [al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 1/403] And 'the hands': i.e., among the conditions is the purification of the place of the hands and the knees on the correct view, and it was chosen by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, and he rejected what was said about the lack of obligation of purifying their place. [Maraqi al-Falah: 209] On the most correct view, and in a narration from Imam (Abu Hanifa) that purification of the place of prostration is not required, i.e., based on the narration permitting sufficing with the nose in prostration, so purification of the place of the nose is not required because it is less than a dirham. [Radd al-Muhtar: 1/403] And covering the awrah: He made it absolute, so it includes whether someone is present or not; even if he prays naked in a dark room while he has a pure garment, it is not permissible by consensus, because covering includes a right of Allah and a right of the people, even if the right of the people is observed overall due to being concealed from them, the right of Allah is not like that. For it might be said: covering is not obligatory with respect to Allah because He sees the covered as He sees the uncovered. The answer is that He sees the uncovered as one abandoning good manners and the covered as one observing good manners, and this good manners is obligatory to observe when capable. [al-Bahr al-Raiq: 1/530]
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah opens the chapter on the conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan) of prayer. The matn states that for prayer to be valid, 27 things are necessary, and then lists some: purification from ritual impurity (hadath), purification of the body, garment, and place from non-excusable impurities, including the location of the feet, hands, knees, and forehead (on the most correct view). Also covering the awrah (private parts) is required; if a woman sees her own awrah from her collar, it does not invalidate the prayer by consensus, but it is against etiquette. The commentary then defines shart and rukn: a shart is something external to the essence that its presence is necessary for validity; a rukn is an integral part of the essence. Conditions are classified into four types: (1) conditions for the validity of initiation only, (2) conditions for validity and continuity, (3) conditions for continuity only (which exist inside prayer, like recitation), and (4) condition for exiting (final sitting). The text notes that the number 27 is not exhaustive; some scholars simplify by mentioning six external conditions and six pillars, but the complete requirement is more. It then addresses specific issues: the place of the hands and knees must be pure on the correct view (chosen by Abu al-Layth), and there is a narration that the place of prostration need not be pure if one can suffice with the nose (since it is less than a dirham). Lastly, covering the awrah is obligatory even if no one is present, because it is a right of Allah and a matter of adab (good manners). This is a definitional and ruling passage, establishing the foundational requirements for prayer.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): In Shariah, it is something on which the existence of another thing depends, but it is external to the essence of that thing. For prayer, it is a prerequisite for validity, such as purification, covering the awrah, facing qibla.
ركن (rukn): In language, the strongest side; in terminology, the part from which the essence is composed. In prayer, pillars include standing, recitation, bowing, prostration, and final sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of shart al-baqa' (condition for continuity)?
A) Intention (niyyah)
B) Facing qibla
C) Recitation (qira'ah) in prayer
D) Final sitting (qa'dah akhirah)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of shurut into four temporal types provides a precise framework for understanding the prerequisites of valid prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Essential Conditions for Valid Prayer: Purity of Place and Covering Awrah
Lists conditions and discusses intra-Hanafi dispute on prostration place purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the key conditions for valid prayer from the matn, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on purity of the place of prostration, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Purity of the place of prostration is required on the strongest view; covering awrah is obligatory even in solitude.

While the previous lesson focused on definitions and categories, this lesson examines specific conditions for prayer listed in the matn: purification from impurity, covering awrah, and especially the dispute about the purity of the place of prostration. The commentary resolves an intra-Hanafi difference and emphasizes the importance of adab (good manners) in covering the awrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions listed in the matn
Read the matn: purification from hadath, purity of body, garment, place (including feet, hands, knees, forehead), and covering awrah. Note that these are from the 27 things required.
The place of prostration includes forehead, nose, hands, knees, feet.
2
Understand the dispute on purity of prostration place
The text mentions a narration from Abu Hanifa that purity is not required based on sufficing with the nose, but the relied-upon view (chosen by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth) is that purity is required for hands, knees, and forehead. The nose area is excused if one uses only the nose.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, resolved by tarjih.
3
Analyze the ruling on covering awrah
Covering awrah is obligatory even when no one is present. The text argues it is a right of Allah and a matter of adab; one must not be uncovered even in darkness.
Consensus (ijma) is cited for the prohibition of praying naked when a garment is available.
4
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view: ensure the place of hands, knees, and forehead is pure. If one prays on a surface with impurity less than a dirham on the nose area, it's excused. Always cover awrah properly.
Practical advice for daily prayer.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة ٧٤ شروط الصلاة وأركانها باب شروط الصلاة وأركانها لابد لصحة الصلاة من سبعة وعشرين شيئا : الطهارة من الحدث، وطهارة الجسد، الأصغر والأكبر والثوب والمكان من نجس غير معفو عنه حتى موضع القدمين، واليدين، والركبتين، كما قدمناه والجبهة على الأصح ، وستر العورة، ولا يضر نظرها من جيبه. إجماعا لكنه خلاف الأدب شروط جمع شرط بسكون الراء، وهو ثلاثة أنواع: عقلي كالقدوم للنجار، وشرعي كالطهارة للصلاة، وجعلي كالدخول المعلق به الطلاق. The 27 Conditions and Pillars of Prayer: Definitions and Categories
Defines conditions and pillars of prayer and their categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the terms shart and rukn according to the Hanafi school and classify the four categories of conditions required for prayer.

Core Idea
Prayer requires 27 elements: external conditions (shurut) and internal pillars (arkan); each has a distinct legal role.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lays the foundational vocabulary for understanding prayer's components. It defines what a condition and a pillar are linguistically and technically, then organizes the conditions into four functional categories. Mastering these definitions is essential for correctly applying the rulings of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
The text introduces 'twenty-seven things' that include both shurut (conditions) and arkan (pillars). Identify which elements fall under each category.
Conditions are external to the act; pillars are internal.
2
Distinguish between shart and rukn
Analyze the linguistic and technical definitions: shart is something whose existence the act depends on but is outside its essence; rukn is a part that composes the essence.
The Hanafi differentiation is key to understanding validity and compensation.
3
Classify the four types of shurut
List the four categories: (1) condition of initiation only, (2) condition of initiation and continuity, (3) condition of continuity only, and (4) condition of exit. Give examples from the text.
Note that some conditions (like recitation) are pillars in themselves but also conditions for continuity.
4
Distinguish existential and non-existential continuity conditions
Within continuity conditions (shart baqa), identify the two subcategories: existential (e.g., recitation) and non-existential (e.g., not preceding the imam).
Non-existential conditions require the absence of something.
5
Understand the scope of the number 27
The text clarifies that 27 is not exhaustive but an approximation. Recognize that shurut and arkan together are all considered furud (obligations).
The phrase 'thing' (shay') encompasses both shart and rukn.

كتاب الصلاة
باب شروط الصلاة وأركانها
لابد لصحة الصلاة من سبعة وعشرين شيئا : الطهارة من الحدث، وطهارة الجسد، الأصغر والأكبر والثوب والمكان من نجس غير معفو عنه حتى موضع القدمين، واليدين، والركبتين، كما قد مناه والجبهة على الأصح ، وستر العورة، ولا يضر نظرها من جيبه. إجماعا لكنه خلاف الأدب
شروط جمع شرط بسكون الراء، وهو ثلاثة أنواع: عقلي كالقدوم للنجار، وشرعي كالطهارة للصلاة، وجعلي كالدخول المعلق به الطلاق. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٦] وهو في الشريعة: ما يتوقف على وجوده الشيء، وهو خارج عن ماهيته. والأركان جمع ركن وهو في اللغة الجانب الأقوى، وفي الاصطلاح: الجزء الذي تتركب الماهية منه ومن غيره. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٠٦]
اعلم ان الشروط من حيث هي أربعة أقسام: (۱) شرط انعقاد لا غير ،كالنية والتحريمة والوقت، والخطبة للجمعة. (۲) وشرط انعقاد ودوام كالطهارة، وستر العورة، واستقبال القبلة. (۳) وشرط بقاء لا غير أي ما يشترط وجوده داخل الصلاة، وهو نوعان أيضا وجودي وعدمي، فالوجودي كالقراءة، فإنها وإن كانت ركنا إلا أنها ركن في نفسها شرط لغيرها؛ لوجودها في كل الأركان تقديرا، ولذا لم يجز استخلاف الأمي ولو بعد أداء فرض القراءة كما في "الدر"، والعدمي كعدم تقدم المقتدي على إمامه وعدم محاذاة مشتهاة في صلاة مشتركة، وعدم تذكر صاحب الترتيب فائتة. (٤) والقسم الرابع: شرط خروج، وهو القعدة الأخيرة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٠٧] وعشرين: لا حصر فيها، ومن اقتصر على ذكر الشروط الستة الخارجة عن الصلاة، وعلى الستة الأركان الداخلة فيها أراد التقريب، وإلا فالمصلي يحتاج إلى ما ذكرناه بزيادة فأردنا به بيان ما إليه الحاجة من شرط صحة الشروع والدوام على صحتها، وكلها فروض وعبر بلفظ الشيء الصادق بالشرط والركن [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٠٧] والمكان أي موضع قدميه أو إحداهما إن رفع الأخرى. [الدر المختار: ٤٠٣/١]
Book of Prayer. Chapter on the conditions and pillars of prayer. For the correctness of prayer, twenty-seven things are necessary: purification from ritual impurity (minor and major), cleanliness of the body, clothes, and place from filth that is not forgiven, even the place of the feet, hands, knees, and forehead on the correct view, covering the private parts, and it does not harm if one looks at it from his collar (if uncovered inadvertently), by consensus, but it is contrary to good manners. 'Shurut' (conditions) is the plural of 'shart' (with sukun on the raa). It has three types: intellectual (like coming for a carpenter), legal (like purity for prayer), and conventional (like the entry upon which divorce is suspended). [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 206] And in the Shariah: the thing upon whose existence the other thing depends, and it is external to its essence. And 'Arkan' (pillars) is the plural of 'rukn'. In language: the strongest side; in terminology: the part from which and from others the essence is composed. [Maraqi al-Falah: 206] Know that the conditions are four categories: (1) Condition of initiation only: like intention, takbir tahrimah, time, and the sermon for Jumu'ah. (2) Condition of initiation and continuity: like purification, covering the private parts, and facing the qiblah. (3) Condition of continuity only: that is, what is required to exist inside the prayer; it is of two types: existential and non-existential. The existential is like recitation; even though it is a pillar, it is a pillar in itself and a condition for others due to its being estimated in every pillar, and therefore it is not allowed for an illiterate person to lead even after performing the obligatory recitation as stated in al-Durr. The non-existential is like the follower not preceding the imam, not aligning with a woman in a joint prayer, and the one with a missed prayer not forgetting it. (4) The fourth category: the condition of exit, which is the last sitting. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 207] And 'twenty-seventh' means there is no count. Whoever mentions only six conditions external to prayer and six internal pillars intends approximation; otherwise the praying person needs what we have mentioned with addition, so we intended to state the need for the condition of validity of initiation and continuity, and all are obligations (furud). And the phrase 'thing' applies to both condition and pillar. [Maraqi al-Falah: 207] And 'place' means the place of his feet or one of them if he raises the other. [al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 1/403]
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a matn definition of the conditions and pillars of prayer. It opens by stating that for prayer to be valid, 27 things are required. It then lists some: purity from hadath, cleanliness of body, clothes, and place (including places of feet, hands, knees, and forehead), covering awrah. It notes that looking at one's own awrah from below the collar does not nullify prayer by consensus but is bad adab. Then it defines the terms 'shart' and 'rukn' linguistically and technically, referencing Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah. It classifies shurut into four types: condition of initiation only (e.g., intention, takbir, time, khutbah for Jumu'ah), condition of initiation and continuity (e.g., purity, covering awrah, qiblah), condition of continuity only (further divided into existential like recitation, and non-existential like not preceding the imam), and condition of exit (last sitting). The text clarifies that the number 27 is not exhaustive; it includes both shurut and arkan, and all are considered obligations (furud). It ends with a note on 'place' meaning the place of the feet.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): What the existence of the act depends on, but is external to its essence.
ركن (rukn): The part from which and with others the essence of the act is composed.
شرط انعقاد (shart in'iqad): A condition required only at the beginning of prayer (initiation), like intention and takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how does a shart (condition) differ from a rukn (pillar)?
A) A shart is external to the act while a rukn is internal.
B) A shart is internal while a rukn is external.
C) Both are the same.
D) A shart is for validity; a rukn is for completion.

Key Takeaway
The 27 things required for prayer include both external conditions (shurut) and internal pillars (arkan); mastering their definitions and categories ensures correct fiqh application.

Facing the Qiblah: Directions for Meccan and Non-Meccan
Explains the obligation of facing the qiblah and its application for different locations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference in qiblah obligation between a Meccan and a non-Meccan, and apply the rule of direction (jihah) for those far from the Ka'bah.

Core Idea
For one who cannot see the Ka'bah, facing the direction (jihah) suffices; for those near, exact alignment may be required.

Facing the qiblah is a condition for prayer. But what does 'facing' mean? Does it require absolute precision? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies: the obligation differs for those who see the Ka'bah and those who don't. Let's examine the rule and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the distinction
The passage states that facing the qiblah is a condition of prayer when able. It then distinguishes between the one who sees the Ka'bah (mushahid) and the one who does not (ghayr al-mushahid). The obligation for the latter is to face the direction (jihah), not necessarily the exact 'ayn.
This distinction is central to the Hanafi position.
2
Define 'direction' (jihah) and its two levels
The text defines jihah as the side which, when faced, aligns the person with the Ka'bah or its airspace. It explains two types: precise alignment (tahqiq) where a line from the face passes through the Ka'bah, and approximate alignment (taqrib) where a slight deviation does not nullify facing due to distance.
The rational proof (dalil aqli) uses geometry to show that at great distances, small deviations are permissible.
3
Apply the principle to Meccan vs non-Meccan
For a Meccan (one in Makkah, especially who can see the Ka'bah), the correct view is that he must face the exact 'ayn, even if inside a house. For the non-Meccan, facing the direction suffices; if obstacles are removed, he is not required to be exactly aligned.
The text cites a weak opinion that treats all Meccans the same, but the relied-upon view distinguishes.
4
Note the weak opinion and why it is rejected
Some scholars said a Meccan in his house should still face the exact Ka'bah if walls were removed. But the author says this is weak. The correct view for a non-Meccan is only direction, not exactness.
This shows the tarjih mechanism within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستقبال القبلة: يعني من شروطها استقبال القبلة عند القدرة البحر الرائق: ٥٥١/١] جهتها: أي بغير المشاهد أنه فرضه إصابة جهة القبلة، وهو الجانب الذي إذا توجه إليه الشخص يكون مسامتا للكعبة أو لهوائها، إما تحقيقا بمعنى أ لو فرض خط من تلقاء وجهه على زاوية قائمة إلى الأفق يكون مارا على الكعبة أو هوائها، وإما تقريبا بمعنى أن يكون الكعبة أو هوائها انحرافا لا تزول به المقابلة بالكلية بأن بقي شيء من سطح الوجه مسامتا لها؛ لأن المقابلة إذا وقعت في مسافة بعيدة لا تزول بما تزول به من الانحراف لو كانت في مسافة قريبة، ويتفاوت ذلك بحسب تفاوت البعد، وتبقى المسامتة انتقال مناسب لذلك البعد، فلو فرض مثلاً من وجه المستقبل للكعبة على التحقيق في بعض البلاد، وخط آخر يقطعه على زاويتين قائمتين من جانب يمين المستقبل وشماله لا تزول تلك المقابلة بالانتقال إلى اليمين والشمال على ذلك الخط بفراسخ كثيرة. [البحر الرائق: ٥٥٢/١] على الصحيح وبعضهم أطلقوا المكي، فشمل من كان معاينتها ومن لم يكن حتى لو صلى مكي في بيته ينبغي أن يصلي بحيث لو أزيلت الجدران يقع استقباله على شطر الكعبة، بخلاف الآفاقي فإنه لو أزيلت الموانع لا يشترط أن يقع استقباله على عين الكعبة لا محالة كذا في "الكافي"، وهو ضعيف. [البحر الرائق: ٥٥٢/١]
And facing the qiblah: meaning among its conditions is facing the qiblah when able to. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/551] Its direction: i.e., for the one who does not see (the Ka'bah), his obligation is to hit the direction of the qiblah. And it is the side that if a person faces it, he is aligned with the Ka'bah or its airspace, either precisely in the sense that if a line is drawn from in front of his face at a right angle to the horizon, it passes over the Ka'bah or its airspace; or approximately in the sense that the Ka'bah or its airspace is in a deviation that does not completely eliminate facing, as long as some part of the surface of the face remains aligned with it. Because facing, when at a long distance, is not nullified by the same deviation that would nullify it at a short distance, and it varies according to the difference in distance, and the alignment remains suitable for that distance. For example, if one supposes a line from the face of one facing the Ka'bah precisely in some country, and another line cutting it at right angles from the right and left side of the one facing, that facing is not removed by moving right or left on that line for many leagues. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/552] According to the correct view, and some scholars include the Meccan broadly, including the one who sees the Ka'bah and the one who does not; so even if a Meccan prays in his house, he should pray such that if walls were removed, his facing would fall on a side of the Ka'bah. Unlike the non-Meccan (afaqi), if obstacles are removed, it is not necessarily required that his facing fall on the exact 'ayn of the Ka'bah. This is in al-Kafi, and it is weak. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/552]
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the condition of facing the qiblah. It establishes that for one who does not see the Ka'bah (ghayr al-mushahid), the obligation is to face the correct direction (jihah), meaning a side which, when faced, aligns the person with the Ka'bah or its airspace. It distinguishes between precise alignment (tahqiq) and approximate alignment (taqrib), explaining that at a distance, a small deviation does not invalidate facing. For a Meccan (someone in Makkah who can see the Ka'bah), the correct view is that he must face the exact 'ayn of the Ka'bah, even if inside his house. For a non-Meccan, if obstacles are removed, he is not required to exactly face the Ka'bah but only the direction. The passage also notes a weak opinion that treats all Meccans alike, requiring exactness only for those who can see it.

Key Terms
الكعبة (al-Ka'bah): The sacred house in Makkah; the direction faced in prayer.
جهة القبلة (jihah al-qiblah): The general direction of the qiblah, not necessarily the exact 'ayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must face the exact 'ayn of the Ka'bah
B) He must face the direction (jihah) of the qiblah
C) He is not required to face qiblah
D) He must face the Ka'bah even if obstacles exist

Key Takeaway
The obligation to face the qiblah differs: Meccans must aim for the exact Ka'bah, while non-Meccans must only face the general direction (jihah).

Time and Intention: Essential Conditions for Prayer
Defines time and intention as conditions of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why time is a condition for prayer and define niyyah as the intent of obedience, covering both actions and abstentions.

Core Idea
Time must be believed to have entered; intention is the heart's resolve to obey Allah.

In this passage, the author notes that many authoritative Hanafi texts omit time from the list of conditions, yet it remains a condition. More importantly, belief in the entry of time is required: if one prays while believing time has not entered, but it actually has, the prayer does not suffice. The passage also defines niyyah as the intent of obedience and seeking nearness to Allah, encompassing both performing and refraining.

Guided Path
1
Identify the status of time in Hanafi texts
Note that several relied-upon works (e.g., al-Quduri) omit mentioning time as a condition, yet the author insists it is a condition. This shows that omission in a matn does not negate the condition.
This is a reminder that not all conditions are always listed in every text.
2
Explain the requirement to believe time has entered
If a person prays while believing the time has not entered, but it actually did, the prayer is invalid. The author explains that the judgment of invalidity was based on the person's own ijtihad (taharrin), and that judgment does not become valid if the opposite appears.
This underscores the importance of certainty about time.
3
Define niyyah in Hanafi fiqh
Niyyah is the intent of obedience and seeking closeness to Allah. It covers all actions of the limbs, whether doing an act or abstaining from it. The heart is the locus of intention.
Hanafis do not require verbalization of the intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[مراقي الفلاح: ٢١٥] واعتقاد دخوله : أي يشترط اعتقاد دخول الوقت حتى لو صلى وعنده أن الوقت لم يدخل فظهر أنه كان قد دخل لا تجزيه؛ لأنه لما حكم بفساد صلاته بناء على دليل شرعي وهو تحريه لا ينقلب جائزاً إذا ظهر خلافه، ويخاف عليه في دينه مراقي الفلاح ۲۱٥] والنية هي في الشرع : قصد الطاعة والتقرب إلى الله تعالى في إيجاد فعل كما في "التلويح"، وهو يعم فعل الجوارح سواء كان إيجاداً أو كفا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢١٥] والتحريمة: اعلم أنهم اختلفوا هل هي شرط أو ركن، فما في بعض الكتب أنها ليست بركن خلافاً لمحمد، فإنه يقول بركنيتها؛ لأنها ذكر مفروض في القيام، فكانت ركناً كالقراءة، وتظهر أثر الثمرة فيما إذا كان حاملاً لنجاسة مانعةٍ فألقاها عند فراغه منها، أو كان منحرفاً عن القبلة فاستقبلها أو مكشوف العورة فسترها بعمل يسير، أو شرع في التكبير قبل ظهور الزوال، ثم ظهر عند الفراغ، فعندهما تجوز صلاته؛ لوجود الأركان مستجمعة للشروط، وتقدم الشروط جائز بالإجماع. ثم اعلم أن لصحة التحريمة خمسة عشر شرطاً ذكر الشيخ منها سبعة، وهي أن تكون التحريمة بلا فاصل، والإتيان قائماً، وعدم تأخير النية عن التحريمة، والنطق بالتحريمة بحيث يسمع نفسه، ونية المتابعة مع نية أصل =
And time: The remembrance of time has been omitted in the chapter on conditions of prayer in several relied-upon works like al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, and al-Kanz, despite their explaining the times, and I do not know the secret of their not mentioning it, although it is described as for performance, a vessel for the performed, and a condition for obligation as established in its place. [Maraqi al-Falah: 215] And belief in its entry: that is, belief in the entry of time is required; so if one prays while thinking the time has not entered, then it appears that it had entered, it does not suffice, because when he judged it to be corrupt based on a legal evidence (his ijtihad), it does not become valid if the opposite appears, and he is feared for his religion. [Maraqi al-Falah: 215] And intention (niyyah) in the Shariah is: the intent of obedience and seeking nearness to Allah in performing an action, as in al-Talwih, and it covers actions of the limbs whether performing or abstaining. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 215] And takbir tahrimah: Know that they differed whether it is a condition or a pillar. What is in some books is that it is not a pillar, contrary to Muhammad (al-Shaybani), who says it is a pillar because it is an obligatory remembrance in standing, so it is a pillar like recitation. The practical effect appears when one was carrying an impurity that prevents (validity) and he throws it away after finishing (the takbir), or he was deviating from the qiblah then faces it, or his awrah was uncovered and he covers it with a small action, or he began the takbir before the time (of zuhr) then it appears after finishing; according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) his prayer is valid because the pillars are complete with conditions (met), and the condition may precede by consensus. Then know that for the validity of takbir tahrimah there are fifteen conditions; the author mentioned seven of them: that the takbir is without interruption, saying it standing, not delaying the intention from the takbir, pronouncing it so that he hears himself, and the intention of following (the imam) with the original intention =
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage discusses three consecutive conditions of prayer: time, intention, and takbir tahrimah. Regarding time, it notes that although many authoritative Hanafi texts omit 'time' from the list of conditions, it is indeed a condition, necessary for performance and a vessel for the act. Belief in the entry of time is required; if one prays based on a mistaken belief that time has not entered, but it actually did, the prayer is not valid because the ruling was based on the evidence he had. Intention (niyyah) is defined as the intent of obedience and drawing near to Allah in performing an act, including both doing and refraining. The discussion of takbir tahrimah is significant: there is a dispute within the Hanafi school between Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad considers takbir tahrimah a pillar (rukn) because it is an obligatory dhikr in standing, analogous to recitation. The practical effect (thamarah) is that if someone begins the takbir while carrying a deterrent impurity, then discards it after finishing the takbir, or turns to the qiblah after starting, or covers his awrah with a small action, or begins takbir before the time then time enters during the prayer — according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the prayer is valid because the conditions can precede the pillars by consensus. The passage then begins listing the conditions for takbir tahrimah itself (there are 15 total, but the author mentions 7), though the text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intent of obedience and seeking closeness to Allah in performing an act, covering both positive actions and abstentions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Time is a condition for prayer, and belief in its entry is essential; intention is defined as the heart's intent to obey Allah.

The Takbir Tahrimah Dispute: Condition or Pillar?
Intra-Hanafi dispute over takbir tahrimah: condition vs. pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the nature of takbir tahrimah and explain the practical difference between considering it a condition versus a pillar.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold takbir tahrimah is a condition; Imam Muhammad holds it is a pillar — the difference affects cases where conditions are met after the takbir.

This passage presents an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah). Imam Muhammad considers it a pillar (rukn), analogous to recitation. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider it a condition (shart), meaning it can precede the pillars. The practical consequence: if one begins the takbir while carrying a deterrent impurity or facing the wrong direction, then corrects it, the prayer is valid according to the majority (the two) but invalid according to Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position on takbir tahrimah
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider takbir tahrimah a condition (shart) for the prayer, not a pillar. This means it is a prerequisite that must be fulfilled before the prayer starts, but its fulfilment can be established after the fact.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad disagrees; he says takbir tahrimah is a pillar (rukn) because it is an obligatory dhikr performed in the standing posture, similar to qira'ah (recitation).
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical effect)
If someone begins the takbir while carrying a deterrent impurity, then discards it after finishing the takbir, or turns to the qiblah after starting, or covers his awrah with a small action, or begins the takbir before the time of prayer then time enters during the prayer — according to the two, the prayer is valid because the conditions can precede the pillars. According to Muhammad, it would be invalid because the pillar (takbir) was performed without the conditions being met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوقت: قد ترك ذكر الوقت في باب شروط الصلاة في عدة من المعتمدات كـ"القدوري" و"المختار"، و"الهداية" و"الكنز" مع بيانهم الأوقات، ولا أعلم سرّ عدم ذكرهم له وإن كان يتصف بأنه للأداء، وظرف للمؤدى، وشرط للوجوب كما هو مقرر في محله. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢١٥] واعتقاد دخوله : أي يشترط اعتقاد دخول الوقت حتى لو صلى وعنده أن الوقت لم يدخل فظهر أنه كان قد دخل لا تجزيه؛ لأنه لما حكم بفساد صلاته بناء على دليل شرعي وهو تحريه لا ينقلب جائزاً إذا ظهر خلافه، ويخاف عليه في دينه مراقي الفلاح ۲۱٥] والنية هي في الشرع : قصد الطاعة والتقرب إلى الله تعالى في إيجاد فعل كما في "التلويح"، وهو يعم فعل الجوارح سواء كان إيجاداً أو كفا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢١٥] والتحريمة: اعلم أنهم اختلفوا هل هي شرط أو ركن، فما في بعض الكتب أنها ليست بركن خلافاً لمحمد، فإنه يقول بركنيتها؛ لأنها ذكر مفروض في القيام، فكانت ركناً كالقراءة، وتظهر أثر الثمرة فيما إذا كان حاملاً لنجاسة مانعةٍ فألقاها عند فراغه منها، أو كان منحرفاً عن القبلة فاستقبلها أو مكشوف العورة فسترها بعمل يسير، أو شرع في التكبير قبل ظهور الزوال، ثم ظهر عند الفراغ، فعندهما تجوز صلاته؛ لوجود الأركان مستجمعة للشروط، وتقدم الشروط جائز بالإجماع. ثم اعلم أن لصحة التحريمة خمسة عشر شرطاً ذكر الشيخ منها سبعة، وهي أن تكون التحريمة بلا فاصل، والإتيان قائماً، وعدم تأخير النية عن التحريمة، والنطق بالتحريمة بحيث يسمع نفسه، ونية المتابعة مع نية أصل =
And time: The remembrance of time has been omitted in the chapter on conditions of prayer in several relied-upon works like al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, and al-Kanz, despite their explaining the times, and I do not know the secret of their not mentioning it, although it is described as for performance, a vessel for the performed, and a condition for obligation as established in its place. [Maraqi al-Falah: 215] And belief in its entry: that is, belief in the entry of time is required; so if one prays while thinking the time has not entered, then it appears that it had entered, it does not suffice, because when he judged it to be corrupt based on a legal evidence (his ijtihad), it does not become valid if the opposite appears, and he is feared for his religion. [Maraqi al-Falah: 215] And intention (niyyah) in the Shariah is: the intent of obedience and seeking nearness to Allah in performing an action, as in al-Talwih, and it covers actions of the limbs whether performing or abstaining. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 215] And takbir tahrimah: Know that they differed whether it is a condition or a pillar. What is in some books is that it is not a pillar, contrary to Muhammad (al-Shaybani), who says it is a pillar because it is an obligatory remembrance in standing, so it is a pillar like recitation. The practical effect appears when one was carrying an impurity that prevents (validity) and he throws it away after finishing (the takbir), or he was deviating from the qiblah then faces it, or his awrah was uncovered and he covers it with a small action, or he began the takbir before the time (of zuhr) then it appears after finishing; according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) his prayer is valid because the pillars are complete with conditions (met), and the condition may precede by consensus. Then know that for the validity of takbir tahrimah there are fifteen conditions; the author mentioned seven of them: that the takbir is without interruption, saying it standing, not delaying the intention from the takbir, pronouncing it so that he hears himself, and the intention of following (the imam) with the original intention =
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage discusses three consecutive conditions of prayer: time, intention, and takbir tahrimah. Regarding time, it notes that although many authoritative Hanafi texts omit 'time' from the list of conditions, it is indeed a condition, necessary for performance and a vessel for the act. Belief in the entry of time is required; if one prays based on a mistaken belief that time has not entered, but it actually did, the prayer is not valid because the ruling was based on the evidence he had. Intention (niyyah) is defined as the intent of obedience and drawing near to Allah in performing an act, including both doing and refraining. The discussion of takbir tahrimah is significant: there is a dispute within the Hanafi school between Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad considers takbir tahrimah a pillar (rukn) because it is an obligatory dhikr in standing, analogous to recitation. The practical effect (thamarah) is that if someone begins the takbir while carrying a deterrent impurity, then discards it after finishing the takbir, or turns to the qiblah after starting, or covers his awrah with a small action, or begins takbir before the time then time enters during the prayer — according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the prayer is valid because the conditions can precede the pillars by consensus. The passage then begins listing the conditions for takbir tahrimah itself (there are 15 total, but the author mentions 7), though the text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intent of obedience and seeking closeness to Allah in performing an act, covering both positive actions and abstentions.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir of prayer (Allahu Akbar) that makes the prayer begin and prohibits worldly acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute over takbir tahrimah?
A) There is no practical difference
B) The prayer is valid if conditions are met after takbir according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
C) The prayer is valid according to Imam Muhammad even if conditions are not met
D) The dispute only affects the reward, not validity

Key Takeaway
Takbir tahrimah is considered a condition by the majority of Hanafi imams, affecting the validity of prayers when conditions are rectified after the takbir.

The Omission of Time in Conditions of Prayer
Commentary on omission of time from conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the omission of time as a condition in early Hanafi texts and explain the commentator's observation regarding this omission.

Core Idea
Time is a condition for prayer, yet several authoritative Hanafi texts omit it in the conditions chapter.

This passage notes a curious feature of many classic Hanafi works: while they later detail the prayer times, they do not mention 'time' as a condition of prayer in the chapter on conditions. The commentator of Maraqi al-Falah points this out and wonders why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The commentator states that time is established as a condition for performance, a container for the performed act, and a condition for obligation. Recognize that time is a necessary condition for prayer validity.
2
Note the omission
List the texts mentioned (al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, al-Kanz) that omitted time from the conditions chapter. Understand that this is a deliberate omission by those authors, the reason for which the commentator does not know.
These are core Hanafi sources (mutamadat).
3
Understand the commentator's stance
The commentator himself considers time a condition. He does not reject the omission but highlights it as a puzzle. Recognize that the omission does not negate the condition; it simply was not mentioned in that specific chapter.
The commentator is from Maraqi al-Falah, a later work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوقت: قد ترك ذكر الوقت في باب شروط الصلاة في عدة من المعتمدات كـ"القدوري" و"المختار"، و"الهداية" و"الكنز" مع بيانهم الأوقات، ولا أعلم سرّ عدم ذكرهم له وإن كان يتصف بأنه للأداء، وظرف للمؤدى، وشرط للوجوب كما هو مقرر في محله. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢١٥] واعتقاد دخوله : أي يشترط اعتقاد دخول الوقت حتى لو صلى وعنده أن الوقت لم يدخل فظهر أنه كان قد دخل لا تجزيه؛ لأنه لما حكم بفساد صلاته بناء على دليل شرعي وهو تحريه لا ينقلب جائزاً إذا ظهر خلافه، ويخاف عليه في دينه [مراقي الفلاح: ٢١٥]
And time: The mention of time in the chapter on conditions of prayer has been omitted in several reliable works like al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, and al-Kanz despite their explanation of the times, and I do not know the secret of their not mentioning it, although it is characterized as [a condition] for performance, a container for the performed act, and a condition for obligation as established in its place. [Maraqi al-Falah: 215] And certainty of its entry: meaning that certainty of the entry of time is required, such that if one prays while believing that the time has not entered, and then it becomes apparent that it had entered, it is not accepted (does not suffice) because when he judged his prayer to be invalid based on a legal evidence, namely his careful estimate (taharrī), it does not become permissible when the opposite becomes apparent, and he fears for his religion. [Maraqi al-Falah: 215]
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage discusses two points: first, the commentator notes that many authoritative texts (mutamadat) like al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, and al-Kanz omitted mentioning time as a condition of prayer in the chapter on conditions, even though they later discuss prayer times. The commentator expresses uncertainty about the reason. Second, he explains that certainty (i'tiqad) of the entry of time is a condition. If a person prays thinking the time has not entered (e.g., he believes it is still before Dhuhr), but it turns out that the time had actually entered, his prayer is not valid. This is because he himself judged it invalid based on his own ijtihad or assumption. Once he considers it invalid according to a shar'i proof (his estimation), the subsequent discovery does not reverse that invalidity.

Key Terms
الوقت (al-waqt): The designated time period for a prayer.
المعتمدات (al-mu'tamadāt): The reliable, authoritative texts in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator of Maraqi al-Falah, why is the omission of time in some Hanafi texts notable?
A) Because it shows that time is not a condition in the Hanafi school.
B) Because those texts still discuss prayer times later, yet omit time in the conditions chapter.
C) Because the commentator disagrees with the omission.
D) Because the texts were not authentic.

Key Takeaway
Time is a condition for prayer even if some authoritative works do not list it in the conditions chapter.

Certainty of Time Entry as a Condition for Prayer
Ruling on condition of certainty for prayer time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that certainty of time entry is a condition for prayer and determine the ruling when a person prays without such certainty.

Core Idea
Certainty of time entry is required: if you pray thinking time hasn't entered, your prayer is invalid even if it had.

This passage establishes that for a prayer to be valid, the person must have certainty (i'tiqad) that the prayer time has entered. Subjective belief at the moment of prayer matters more than objective reality. If one prays while thinking the time has not yet come, and later discovers it had, the prayer is not accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The text states: 'certainty of its entry is required'. Identify that this is a condition (shart) for the validity of the prayer.
2
Understand the scenario
Consider a person who prays while believing that the time has not entered (e.g., he thinks it is still before Dhuhr). Later it becomes clear that the time had actually started.
The belief is based on his own estimation (taharrī).
3
Apply the ruling
The text says such a prayer 'does not suffice' (la tujzī'uhu). That is, it is invalid and must be repeated. The person's initial ruling of invalidity (based on his own judgment) cannot be overturned by later discovery.
The reason: his taharrī is a shar'i evidence; once he acts on it, reality does not change his accountability.
4
Note the consequence
The person 'fears for his religion' because he deliberately prayed without certainty of time. This highlights the sinfulness of praying without due caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Once he considers it invalid according to a shar'i proof (his estimation), the subsequent discovery does not reverse that invalidity.

Definition and Legal Ruling of Intention in Prayer
Defining intention in Islamic law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of niyyah and explain its status as a condition for prayer.

Core Idea
Intention is the heart's resolve to obey Allah; it is a condition, not a pillar.

Intention (niyyah) is foundational to every act of worship in Islam. In this lesson, we examine its precise definition according to the Hanafi school, drawing from the text of al-Talwih. We will also clarify its legal status as a mandatory condition (shart) for the validity of prayer, distinguishing it from other elements like pillars.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the act and category
Recognize that niyyah pertains to acts of worship (ibadat), specifically prayer (salah). It is not a physical action but a mental resolve.
Intention is an internal act of the heart.
2
2. State the Shari'i definition
Memorize the definition: 'The resolve to obey and draw close to Allah Almighty in performing an action.' Note that it includes both doing and refraining.
The definition covers positive acts (e.g., praying) and negative acts (e.g., fasting by abstaining).
3
3. Recognize its scope
Understand that intention applies to all actions of the limbs (jawarih), whether it is performing an act or refraining from it.
This broad scope ensures that refrainment with intention is also an act of worship.
4
4. Identify the legal ruling
According to the Hanafi school, intention is wajib (obligatory) as a condition for the validity of prayer. Without intention, the prayer is invalid.
The ruling is not fard because the proof is zanni; but it is confirmed as wajib.
5
5. Distinguish common misconceptions
Note that intention is not required to be spoken; it is a resolve in the heart. Vocalization is recommended in other schools but not required in Hanafi.
This distinction is important for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنية هي في الشرع : قصد الطاعة والتقرب إلى الله تعالى في إيجاد فعل كما في "التلويح"، وهو يعم فعل الجوارح سواء كان إيجاداً أو كفا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢١٥]
And intention in Islamic law is: the resolve to obey and draw close to Allah Almighty in performing an action, as in al-Talwih, and it includes actions of the limbs, whether it is doing something or refraining. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 215]
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage provides a concise definition of niyyah (intention) as used in the Shari'ah. It is not a mere mental thought but a firm resolve (qasd) to perform an act with the purpose of obedience and drawing closer to Allah. The definition from al-Talwih emphasizes that it applies to both positive actions (doing) and negative actions (refraining, kaff). This definition is broad enough to cover all acts of worship.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The resolve to obey and seek nearness to Allah in performing an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only actions that are done physically.
B) Both doing and refraining.
C) Only acts of worship like prayer.
D) Only intentions of fasting.

Key Takeaway
Intention is the heart's resolve to obey Allah, encompassing both action and inaction; it is a required condition for the validity of prayer in the Hanafi school.
