Takbir Tahrimah: Shart or Rukn? Conditions for Validity
Intra-Hanafi dispute and conditions of takbir tahrimah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute over takbir tahrimah (shart vs rukn), identify the practical consequences, and list the essential conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Takbir tahrimah is the key that opens prayer; its nature as condition or pillar changes ruling when a defect is corrected after starting.

In this passage from Nur al-Idah, the author tackles a fundamental question: Is the opening 'Allahu Akbar' a condition (shart) that must be present at the start, or a pillar (rukn) that requires all conditions from the moment it is uttered? The answer has real-world consequences, as illustrated by examples of correcting impurities, direction, or covering after beginning. The passage then lists fifteen conditions for a valid takbir, clarifying each with detailed rulings from the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider takbir tahrimah a condition (shart) for the prayer, while Muhammad al-Shaybani considers it a pillar (rukn). This distinction affects the need for conditions at the moment of the takbir.
The text states: 'they differed whether it is a condition or a pillar. In some books it is not a pillar, contrary to Muhammad.'
2
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah)
Consider the example: if someone had a ritually impure object on him and discards it after saying the takbir, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf the prayer is valid because the pillars of prayer are present with conditions fulfilled later, but according to Muhammad the takbir itself is a pillar requiring immediate conditions, so it would not be valid.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf — the practical difference in rulings.
3
List the conditions for validity
The passage mentions fifteen conditions, of which seven are explicitly listed. Focus on those seven: (1) no interruption between intention and takbir, (2) performing it standing, (3) not delaying intention after takbir, (4) pronouncing it audibly enough to hear oneself, (5) intention of following for the follower, (6) specifying the obligatory prayer, (7) specifying the type (fard/wajib) if necessary.
The text also adds more conditions like Arabic language, correct pronunciation without elongation of hamza or ba, complete sentence, etc.
4
Analyze the detailed conditions
Work through the specific rulings on intention (actual vs. legal accompaniment), standing (including catching the imam in ruku), and pronunciation (mute person, deaf person, noise). Note the distinctions between actions that break the connection (eating, drinking, speech) and those that do not (walking, wudu).
The commentary explains each condition with examples from later sections of Maraqui al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario like: a person begins takbir while facing away from qibla but turns during the takbir before finishing. Determine validity under each view. According to the shart view (Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf), the condition of facing qibla can be corrected after starting, so the prayer is valid. According to the rukn view (Muhammad), the takbir itself requires facing qibla at its utterance, so it would be invalid.
This reflects the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتحريمة: اعلم أنهم اختلفوا هل هي شرط أو ركن، فما في بعض الكتب أنها ليست بركن خلافاً لمحمد، فإنه يقول بركنيتها؛ لأنها ذكر مفروض في القيام، فكانت ركناً كالقراءة، وتظهر أثر الثمرة فيما إذا كان حاملاً لنجاسة مانعةٍ فألقاها عند فراغه منها، أو كان منحرفاً عن القبلة فاستقبلها أو مكشوف العورة فسترها بعمل يسير، أو شرع في التكبير قبل ظهور الزوال، ثم ظهر عند الفراغ، فعندهما تجوز صلاته؛ لوجود الأركان مستجمعة للشروط، وتقدم الشروط جائز بالإجماع. ثم اعلم أن لصحة التحريمة خمسة عشر شرطاً ذكر الشيخ منها سبعة، وهي أن تكون التحريمة بلا فاصل، والإتيان قائماً، وعدم تأخير النية عن التحريمة، والنطق بالتحريمة بحيث يسمع نفسه، ونية المتابعة مع نية أصل بالتحريمة. بلا فاصل والإتيان بالتحريمة قائما قبل انحنائه للركوع، وعدم تأخير النية عن التحريمة، والنطق بالتحريمة بحيث يُسْمِعُ نفسه على الأصح ونية المتابعة من الجلالة الصلاة للمقتدي، وتعيين الفرض وتعيين الواجب وكونها بلفظ العربية للقادر عليها في الصحيح، وأن لا يمد همزة فيها، ولا باء أكبر، وأن يأتي بجملة تامة، وأن يكون بذكر خالص الله تعالى وأن لا يكون بالبسملة، وأن لا يحذف الهاء من الجلالة، وأن يأتي بالهاوي والمراد بالهاوي الألف الناشي بالمد الذي في اللام الثانية . فإذا حذفه الحالف، أو الذابح، أو المكبر الصلاة، أو حذف الهاء من الجلالة اختلف في انعقاد يمينه، وحل ذبيحته، وصحة تحريمته، فلا يترك ذلك احتياطاً، وأن لا يقرن التكبير بما يفسده، فلا يفسد مشروعه لو قال: " الله أكبر العالم بالمعدوم والموجود، أو العالم بأحوال الخلق"؛ لأنه يشبه كلام الناس. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢١٧] بلا فاصل: أي الأول من شروط صحة التحريمة أن توجد مقارنة للنية حقيقة أو حكماً بلا فاصل بينها وبين النية بأجنبي يمنع الاتصال كالأكل والشرب والكلام، فأما المشي للصلاة والوضوء فليسا مانعين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢١٧] ومثال المقارنة حقيقةً: أن ينوي مقارناً للشروع بالتكبير، ومثال المقارنة الحكمية: أن يقدم النية على الشروع، قالوا: لو نوى عند الوضوء أنه يصلي الظهر مثلاً و لم يشتغل بعد النية بعمل يدل على الإعراض كأكل وشرب وكلام ونحوها، ثم انتهى إلى محل الصلاة و لم تحضره النية، جازت صلاته بالنية السابقة [مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢١٧] قائما: فإن قلت: لما كان القيام شرطا لصحة التحريمة فكيف يصح تحريمة من صلى قاعدا متنفلا أو مفترضا لعذر؟ قلت: أراد قائما حقيقة أو حكما فيما يفترض له القيام فالمتنفل قاعدا لا يفترض عليه القيام، والقاعد عذرا قائم حكما قبل انحنائه إلخ أي قبل وجود انحنائه بما هو أقرب للركوع، قال في "البرهان": لو أدرك الإمام راكعاً فحنى ظهره ثم كبر، إن كان إلى القيام أقرب بأن لا تنال يداه ركبتيه صح الشروع ولو أراد به تكبير الركوع، وتلغو نيته؛ لأن مدرك الإمام في الركوع لا يحتاج إلى تكبير مرتين خلافا لبعضهم وإن كان إلى الركوع أقرب بأن تنال يداه ركبتيه لا يصح الشروع [مراقي الفلاح (۲۱۸] والنطق بالتحريمة ولا يلزم الأخرس تحريك لسانه على الصحيح، وغير الأخرس يشترط سماع نفسه. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۱۹] يسمع يسمع يسمع نفسه: أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن به صمم، أما لو كان به صمم أو كانت جلبة الأصوات، فالشرط أن يكون بحيث لو أزيل المانع لأمكن السماع [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۱۹] الأصح وأكثر المشايخ على أن الصحيح أن الجهر حقيقة أن غيره، والمخافتة أن نفسه. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۱۹] ونية المتابعة أي لابد لصحة صلاة المقتدي أن ينوي المتابعة، واعلم أن الصلاة التي يدخل فيها إما أن تكون فرضاً أو غيره، والثاني يكفي فيه مطلق النية نفلاً كانت أو سنةً في الصحيح؛ لأن النية في النفل للتمييز عن العادة، وهو يحصل بمطلق النية، وقولنا: "في الصحيح" احتراز عما قيل: إنه لابد من أن ينوي سنة الرسول الصحة والسلا؛ لأن فيها صفة زائدة على النفل المطلق كالفرض، والأول: إما أن يكون المصلي فيه منفرداً أو مقتدياً بالإمام والمنفرد يلزمه تعيين الفرض الذي يدخل فيه كالظهر مثلاً، ولا يكفيه أن يقول : نويت الفرض لاختلاف الفروض؛ فلابد من التمييز. [العناية: ٣٣٢/١]
And the Takbir Tahrimah: Know that they differed whether it is a condition or a pillar. In some books it is stated that it is not a pillar, contrary to Muhammad, who says it is a pillar because it is a remembrance prescribed while standing, so it becomes a pillar like recitation. The practical effect appears in the case where one was carrying a preventing impurity and threw it away upon finishing [the takbir], or was deviating from the qibla and then faced it, or had his awrah exposed and covered it with minimal action, or began the takbir before the time entered and then it became apparent after finishing; according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) his prayer is valid because the pillars are present fulfilling the conditions, and presenting conditions is permissible by consensus. Then know that for the validity of the takbir tahrimah there are fifteen conditions, the Sheikh mentioned seven of them: that the takbir occur without interruption, performing it standing, not delaying the intention from the takbir, pronouncing the takbir such that he can hear himself, and the intention of following [the imam] along with the basic intention for the takbir. Without interruption and coming with the takbir standing before bowing for ruku, not delaying the intention from the takbir, pronouncing the takbir so that he can hear himself according to the most correct view, and the intention of following for the follower, specifying the obligatory and specifying the duty, and it being in the Arabic language for one able to do so according to the correct view, and that he not prolong the hamza nor the ba' of 'Akbar', and that he come with a complete sentence, and that it be with pure remembrance of Allah and not with the basmalah, and that he not omit the ha' from the word of majesty (Allah), and that he bring the 'hawi' which is the alif originating from elongation in the second lam. If a swearer omits it, or a slaughterer, or one saying takbir for prayer, or omits the ha' from the word of majesty, there is a difference in the validity of his oath, the permissibility of his slaughtered animal, and the validity of his takbir tahrimah, so it should not be left as a precaution. And that he not combine the takbir with something that corrupts it, so it does not invalidate his undertaking if he says 'Allahu Akbar al-alim bil ma'dum wal mawjud' or 'al-alim bi ahwal al-khalq' because it resembles the speech of people. [Maraqi al-Falah: 217] Without interruption: meaning the first of the conditions for the validity of the takbir tahrimah is that it be accompanied by the intention actually or legally without interruption between it and the intention by something extraneous that prevents connection like eating, drinking, or speech. As for walking for prayer and wudu, they are not preventives. [Maraqi al-Falah: 217] An example of actual accompaniment: that he intends concurrently with commencing the takbir. An example of legal accompaniment: that he advances the intention before commencement. They said: if he intends at the time of wudu that he will pray Dhuhr for example, and after the intention he does not engage in an act indicating turning away like eating, drinking, speech, etc., then he reaches the place of prayer and the intention does not come to him, his prayer is valid with the previous intention. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 217] Standing: if you say: since standing is a condition for the validity of takbir, how does the takbir of one who prays sitting as a voluntary or obligatory prayer due to an excuse become valid? I say: He intended standing in reality or legally for that for which standing is obligatory; the one who prays sitting voluntarily is not obligated to stand, and the one who sits due to an excuse is legally standing before his bending etc., meaning before his bending to what is closer to ruku. Al-Burhan said: If one finds the imam in ruku and bends his back then says takbir, if he is closer to standing such that his hands do not reach his knees, the commencement is valid even if he intended by it the takbir of ruku, and his intention is nullified because one who catches the imam in ruku does not need to say takbir twice, contrary to some. But if he is closer to ruku such that his hands reach his knees, the commencement is not valid. [Maraqi al-Falah: 218] And the pronunciation of the takbir: the mute person is not required to move his tongue according to the correct view, and for the non-mute it is a condition to hear himself. [Maraqi al-Falah: 219] 'Hear himself': it is unrestricted and is restricted to when there is no deafness; if he is deaf or there is noise, the condition is that if the obstacle were removed, hearing would be possible. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 219] The most correct and the majority of scholars hold that the correct view is that loudness is in reality that someone else hears, and quietness is that he hears himself. [Maraqi al-Falah: 219] And the intention of following: meaning for the validity of the prayer of the follower, he must intend to follow. Know that the prayer one enters into is either obligatory or other. For the other, a mere intention suffices, whether it is a nafl or sunnah according to the correct view, because the intention in nafl is for distinguishing from habit, and that is achieved by mere intention. Our saying 'according to the correct view' is a caveat against what was said: that one must intend the sunnah of the Messenger for validity and soundness because it has an additional quality over absolute nafl like the obligatory. For the first (obligatory prayer), either the person is praying alone or following an imam. The one alone must specify the obligatory prayer he is entering, like Dhuhr for example, and it is not sufficient for him to say 'I intend the obligatory' because of the difference of obligations; therefore specification is necessary. [Al-Inayah: 1/332]
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage comprehensively discusses the takbir tahrimah (the opening 'Allahu Akbar' of prayer). It begins with an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider it a condition (shart) for prayer, while Muhammad al-Shaybani considers it a pillar (rukn). The commentator provides practical examples showing the difference: if someone has an impurity on his person and discards it after saying the takbir, or turns to the qibla after deviation, or covers his awrah after starting, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf the prayer is valid because the pillars were fulfilled with the conditions present later, but according to Muhammad it is not valid because the takbir itself is a pillar that requires all conditions at its moment. Then the text lists fifteen conditions for the validity of the takbir, mentioning seven: (1) no interruption between intention and takbir, (2) performing it while standing (with explanation for excused cases), (3) not delaying intention after takbir, (4) pronouncing it audibly enough to hear oneself (with details for the deaf or noisy environments), (5) intention of following for the follower, (6) specifying the specific prayer for the one who is alone or the imam, and (7) specifying the type (fard or wajib) for the follower? Actually the text mentions more than seven in the detail. The passage then elaborates on each condition: the meaning of 'without interruption' (bila fasil) distinguishes between actions that break connection (eating, drinking, speech) and those that don't (walking, wudu). It explains actual versus legal simultaneity of intention. It addresses the issue of standing: for a person who catches the imam in ruku, bending with hands reaching knees affects validity. For pronunciation, a mute person is exempt from moving his tongue, but a non-mute must hear himself. The strongest view distinguishes loud (jahr) as being heard by others and low (mukhaftah) as hearing oneself. Finally, the text discusses the intention of following: for supererogatory prayers, a general intention suffices, but for obligatory prayers, one must specify which prayer (like Dhuhr) and whether one is praying alone or following. The passage is rich in legal detail and shows the precision of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening 'Allahu Akbar' that initiates the prayer, considered by some as a condition and by others as a pillar.
الهاوي (al-hāwī): The alif that originates from elongation in the final lam of the word 'Allah' when written in Arabic script.
نية المتابعة (niyyat al-mutāba'ah): The intention of following the imam that a follower must have for the validity of his prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the practical difference between considering takbir tahrimah as a rukn (as Muhammad holds) and as a shart (as Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold)?
A) No practical difference.
B) If a person starts takbir while facing away from qibla, then turns to qibla, the prayer is valid according to Muhammad but not according to Abu Hanifa.
C) If a person had a ritually impure object and discards it after takbir, prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf but not according to Muhammad.
D) Muhammad allows speaking during takbir, while others do not.

Key Takeaway
Takbir tahrimah is a condition (shart) in the relied-upon Hanafi view, allowing correction of certain conditions after its utterance, which saves the prayer from repetition.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Conditions for the Validity of the Opening Takbir (Tahrima) in Prayer
Listing and explaining the conditions for the opening takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list all the conditions for the validity of the opening takbir and explain the Hanafi reasoning behind each condition.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is valid only when its conditions are met – from intention and standing to Arabic pronunciation.

The tahrima is the gateway to prayer; if it is not valid, the entire prayer is invalid. The Hanafi school has detailed the conditions that must be present for the tahrima to be sound. This lesson presents those conditions as listed in Nur al-Idah, along with clarifications from the commentaries of Maraqi al-Falah and its Hashiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition: no gap between intention and takbir
The intention must be concurrent with the takbir, either in reality or legally. Any act that breaks continuity (eating, drinking, speech) invalidates the connection, but walking or making wudu does not.
Legal concurrence means if the intention is made before, as long as no turning-away act occurs, the connection holds.
2
Analyze the standing condition and its exceptions
The takbir must be pronounced while standing if one is able. For a nafl prayer, sitting is permissible. For one with an excuse, standing is considered fulfilled if the bend is less than the ruku' position. If one catches the imam in ruku', the hands-not-reaching-knees rule determines validity.
The definition of standing is that when the arms are extended, the hands do not reach the knees.
3
Examine the pronunciation and language conditions
The takbir must be in Arabic if able, pronounce each part correctly (no lengthening of hamza or ba'), be a complete sentence, be purely the mention of Allah (not mixed with basmala or other words), and not omit the ha' of 'Allah'. The follower must be able to hear himself (or be able to if deaf/noisy).
The mute is excused from moving the tongue.
4
Understand the requirement of specifying the type of prayer
For a fard prayer, the performer must specify which fard (e.g., Zuhr) in the intention. For a wajib like witr, some scholars require specifying it as wajib, but for Eid and witr, specification without the term 'wajib' is acceptable. For nafl, absolute intention suffices.
Precaution is to specify for all prayers.
5
Apply conditions to the follower and consider recitation
The muqtadi must intend to follow the imam. The imam must intend to lead for male followers. In recitation, at least one verse of two words is required in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all rak'ahs of nafl and witr. The muqtadi listens silently; reciting is makruh tahrimi.
The condition of standing applies to non-nafl prayers.

Source Text

بلا فاصل والإتيان بالتحريمة قائما قبل انحنائه للركوع، وعدم تأخير النية عن التحريمة، والنطق بالتحريمة بحيث يُسْمِعُ نفسه على الأصح ونية المتابعة للمقتدي، وتعيين الفرض وتعيين الواجب وكونها بلفظ العربية للقادر عليها في الصحيح، وأن لا يمد همزة فيها، ولا باء أكبر، وأن يأتي بجملة تامة، وأن يكون بذكر خالص الله تعالى وأن لا يكون بالبسملة، وأن لا يحذف الهاء من الجلالة، وأن يأتي بالهاوي والمراد بالهاوي الألف الناشي بالمد الذي في اللام الثانية . فإذا حذفه الحالف، أو الذابح، أو المكبر الصلاة، أو حذف الهاء من الجلالة اختلف في انعقاد يمينه، وحل ذبيحته، وصحة تحريمته، فلا يترك ذلك احتياطاً، وأن لا يقرن التكبير بما يفسده، فلا يفسد مشروعه لو قال: " الله أكبر العالم بالمعدوم والموجود، أو العالم بأحوال الخلق"؛ لأنه يشبه كلام الناس. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢١٧] بلا فاصل: أي الأول من شروط صحة التحريمة أن توجد مقارنة للنية حقيقة أو حكماً بلا فاصل بينها وبين النية بأجنبي يمنع الاتصال كالأكل والشرب والكلام، فأما المشي للصلاة والوضوء فليسا مانعين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢١٧] ومثال المقارنة حقيقةً: أن ينوي مقارناً للشروع بالتكبير، ومثال المقارنة الحكمية: أن يقدم النية على الشروع، قالوا: لو نوى عند الوضوء أنه يصلي الظهر مثلاً و لم يشتغل بعد النية بعمل يدل على الإعراض كأكل وشرب وكلام ونحوها، ثم انتهى إلى محل الصلاة و لم تحضره النية، جازت صلاته بالنية السابقة [مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢١٧] قائما: فإن قلت: لما كان القيام شرطا لصحة التحريمة فكيف يصح تحريمة من صلى قاعدا متنفلا أو مفترضا لعذر؟ قلت: أراد قائما حقيقة أو حكما فيما يفترض له القيام فالمتنفل قاعدا لا يفترض عليه القيام، والقاعد عذرا قائم حكما قبل انحنائه إلخ أي قبل وجود انحنائه بما هو أقرب للركوع، قال في "البرهان": لو أدرك الإمام راكعاً فحنى ظهره ثم كبر، إن كان إلى القيام أقرب بأن لا تنال يداه ركبتيه صح الشروع ولو أراد به تكبير الركوع، وتلغو نيته؛ لأن مدرك الإمام في الركوع لا يحتاج إلى تكبير مرتين خلافا لبعضهم وإن كان إلى الركوع أقرب بأن تنال يداه ركبتيه لا يصح الشروع [مراقي الفلاح (۲۱۸] والنطق بالتحريمة ولا يلزم الأخرس تحريك لسانه على الصحيح، وغير الأخرس يشترط سماع نفسه. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۱۹] يسمع نفسه: أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن به صمم، أما لو كان به صمم أو كانت جلبة الأصوات، فالشرط أن يكون بحيث لو أزيل المانع لأمكن السماع [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۱۹] الأصح وأكثر المشايخ على أن الصحيح أن الجهر حقيقة أن غيره، والمخافتة أن نفسه. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۱۹] ونية المتابعة أي لابد لصحة صلاة المقتدي أن ينوي المتابعة، واعلم أن الصلاة التي يدخل فيها إما أن تكون فرضاً أو غيره، والثاني يكفي فيه مطلق النية نفلاً كانت أو سنةً في الصحيح؛ لأن النية في النفل للتمييز عن العادة، وهو يحصل بمطلق النية، وقولنا: "في الصحيح" احتراز عما قيل: إنه لابد من أن ينوي سنة الرسول الصحة والسلا؛ لأن فيها صفة زائدة على النفل المطلق كالفرض، والأول: إما أن يكون المصلي فيه منفرداً أو مقتدياً بالإمام والمنفرد يلزمه تعيين الفرض الذي يدخل فيه كالظهر مثلاً، ولا يكفيه أن يقول : نويت الفرض لاختلاف الفروض؛ فلابد من التمييز. [العناية: ٣٣٢/١] للمقتدي، وتعيين الفرض، وتعيين الواجب ولا يشترط التعيين في النفل، والقيام في غير النفل، والقراءة ولو آية في ركعتي الفرض وكل النفل والوتر، ولم يتعين شيء من القرآن لصحة الصلاة، ولا يقرأ المؤتم بل يستمع وينصت، وإن قرأ كره تحريما، للمقتدي: أطلق في اشتراط نية المتابعة فشمل الجمعة، لكن في "الذخيرة" و "فتاوى قاضي خان": لو نوى الجمعة و لم ينو الاقتداء بالإمام فإنه يجوز؛ لأن الجمعة لا تكون إلا مع الإمام، وأفاد أن تعيين الإمام ليس بشرط في صحة الاقتداء، فلو نوى الاقتداء بالإمام وهو يظن أنه زيد فإذا هو عمرو يصح، إلا إذا نوى الاقتداء بزيد فإذا هو عمرو فإنه لا يصح؛ لأن العبرة لما نوى، وقيد بـ"المقتدي"؛ لأن الإمام يشترط في صحة اقتداء الرجال به نية الإمامة؛ لأنه منفرد في حق نفسه، ألا ترى أنه لو حلف أن لا يؤم أحداً، فصلى ونوى أن لا يؤم أحداً فصلى خلفه جماعة لم يحنث؛ لأن شرط الحنث أن يقصد الإمامة و لم يوجد. [البحر الرائق: ٥٥٠/١] وتعيين الفرض: أي السادس من شروط التحريمة تعيين الفرض في ابتداء الشروع، حتى لو نوى فرضاً وشرع فيه، ثم نسي فظنه تطوعاً فأتمه على ظنه، فهو فرض مسقط، وكذا عكسه يكون تطوعاً. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٢] وتعيين الواجب : أطلقه فشمل قضاء نفل أفسده والنذر والوتر وركعتي الطواف والعيدين لاختلاف الأسباب، وقالوا في العيدين والوتر: ينوي صلاة العيد والوتر من غير تقييد بالواجب، ليس المراد أنه ممنوع عن نية الواجب، بل أنه لا يلزمه ذلك للاختلاف [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٢٢] في النفل: أراد بالنفل ما يعم السنن، فشمل سنة الفجر أيضًا، وكذا التراويح عند عامة المشايخ، وهو الصحيح، والاحتياط التعيين، فينوي مراعياً صفتها بالتراويح أو سنة الوقت. والقيام إلخ: أطلقه وهو مقيد بمن إذا قدر عليه وعلى الركوع والسجود ولا يفوته بقيامه شرط طهارة مثلاً، ولا قدرة القراءة، فلو تعسّر عليه القيام أو قدر عليه وعجز عن السجود لا يلزمه، لكنه يخير في الثانية بين الإيماء قائماً أو قاعداً كما لو كان معه جرح يسيل إذا سجد، فإنه يخير كذلك، ولو كان بحيث لو قام سلس بوله، أو لو قام ينكشف من العورة ما يمنع الصلاة، أو يعجز عن القراءة حال القيام وفي القعود لا يحصل شيء من ذلك يجب القعود، وكذا إن كان بحيث لو صلى قاعداً قدر على الإتمام وقائماً .لا. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٢٤] وحد القيام أن يكون بحيث إذا مد يديه لا ينال ركبتيه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٤] ولو آية: أي ولو قرأ آية قصيرةً مركبةً من كلمتين كقوله تعالى: ثُمَّ نَظَرَ [المدثر : ٢١] في ظاهر الرواية، وأما الآية التي هي كلمة كــمُدْهَامَّتَانِ (الرحمن: ٦٤) أو حرف كـ خاص [؟] ، فون [؟] ، ورق [؟] أو حرفان فقد اختلف المشايخ، والأصح أنه لا تجوز بها الصلاة. [ مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٥، ٢٢٦]
Without a gap and performing the tahrima standing before his bending for ruku', and not delaying the intention after the tahrima, and uttering the tahrima such that he makes himself hear according to the most correct view, and the intention of following for the muqtadi, and specifying the obligatory prayer, and specifying the wajib, and it being in the Arabic language for the one able to do so according to the correct view, and that he does not lengthen its hamza, nor the ba' of 'Akbar', and that he comes with a complete sentence, and that it is a pure mention of Allah the Exalted and that it is not with the basmala, and that he does not omit the ha' from the word of majesty, and that he comes with the 'alif' which is the alif arising from the lengthening in the second lam. So if the one swearing, or the one slaughtering, or the one saying takbir in prayer omits it, or omits the ha' from the word of majesty, there is disagreement concerning the validity of his oath, the permissibility of his slaughtered animal, and the soundness of his tahrima, so one should not leave that as a precaution. And that he does not connect the takbir with something that spoils it, so what he begins is not spoiled if he says: 'Allah is greater, the Knower of the non-existent and the existent, or the Knower of the states of creation'; because it resembles human speech. [Maraqi al-Falah: 217] Without a gap: meaning the first of the conditions for the soundness of the tahrima is that it occurs concurrent with the intention, in reality or legally, without a gap between it and the intention by a foreign element that prevents connection like eating, drinking, and speech. As for walking for prayer and wudu', they are not preventers. [Maraqi al-Falah: 217] And an example of concurrent in reality is that he intends concurrent with beginning the takbir. And an example of concurrent legally is that he places the intention before beginning. They said: if he intended at the time of wudu' that he will pray Zuhr, for example, and after the intention he did not occupy himself with an act indicating turning away like eating, drinking, speech, and the like, then he reached the place of prayer and the intention did not occur to him, his prayer is permissible with the previous intention. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 217] Standing: if you say: since standing is a condition for the soundness of the tahrima, how is the tahrima of one who prays sitting as a nafl or out of necessity considered sound? I say: He intended standing in reality or legally in that which standing is obligatory for him. For the one praying nafl sitting, standing is not obligatory upon him, and the one sitting out of necessity is considered standing legally before his bending, etc., meaning before the occurrence of his bending which is closer to ruku'. He said in al-Burhan: if he catches the imam in ruku' and bends his back then says takbir, if he is closer to standing such that his hands do not reach his knees, the commencement is sound even if he intended it as the takbir for ruku', and his intention is void; because the one who catches the imam in ruku' does not need to say takbir twice, contrary to some. And if he is closer to ruku' such that his hands reach his knees, commencement is not sound. [Maraqi al-Falah (218)] And uttering the tahrima: and the mute is not required to move his tongue according to the correct view, and for other than the mute, hearing himself is a condition. [Maraqi al-Falah: 219] Hearing himself: he made it absolute, but it is restricted to when he is not deaf. However, if he is deaf or there is loud noise, the condition is that it is such that if the obstacle were removed, he would be able to hear. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 219] The correct view and most mashayikh hold that the correct view is that loud (jahr) is that he makes others hear, and quiet (mukhafata) is that he makes himself hear. [Maraqi al-Falah: 219] And intention of following: i.e., for the soundness of the prayer of the muqtadi, he must intend following. Know that the prayer he enters into is either obligatory or other than it. For the second, absolute intention suffices, whether it is nafl or sunnah according to the correct view; because intention in nafl is for distinction from custom, and that is achieved by absolute intention. And our saying 'according to the correct view' is a reservation against what has been said: that he must intend the sunnah of the Messenger, peace and blessings be upon him; because it has an additional quality over absolute nafl like the obligatory. As for the first: either the worshipper is praying alone or following an imam. The one praying alone is required to specify the obligatory prayer he enters into, like Zuhr for example, and it does not suffice him to say 'I intend the obligatory' because of the difference of obligatory prayers; so specification is necessary. [al-Inayah: 1/332] For the muqtadi, and specifying the fard, and specifying the wajib, and specification is not required in nafl, and standing in other than nafl, and recitation of at least one verse in the two rak'ahs of fard and all nafl and witr, and no specific thing from the Quran is determined for the validity of the prayer. And the muqtadi does not recite but listens and remains silent, and if he recites it is makruh tahrimi. For the muqtadi: he made it absolute in stipulating the intention of following, so it includes Friday prayer. But in al-Dhakhira and Fatawa Qadhi Khan: if he intended Friday and did not intend following the imam, it is permissible; because Friday cannot be except with an imam. And he indicated that specifying the imam is not a condition for the validity of following. So if he intended following the imam thinking it is Zayd and it turned out to be Amr, it is valid, except if he intended following Zayd and it turned out to be Amr, then it is not valid; because consideration is given to what he intended. And he restricted it to 'the muqtadi' because for the imam, for the validity of men following him, intention of imamah is a condition; because he is alone with regard to himself. Do you not see that if he swore that he would never lead anyone, then he prayed and intended not to lead anyone, and people prayed behind him, he does not break his oath; because the condition for breaking the oath is that he intends imamah, and that was not present. [al-Bahr al-Raiq: 1/550] And specifying the fard: meaning the sixth of the conditions of the tahrima is specifying the fard at the beginning of the commencement, so if he intended an obligatory prayer and began it, then forgot and thought it was voluntary and completed it with that thought, it is an obligatory prayer that has served the purpose, and likewise the reverse would be voluntary. [Maraqi al-Falah: 222] And specifying the wajib: he made it absolute, so it includes making up a spoiled nafl, and vows, and witr, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf, and the two Eids due to the difference of causes. And they said regarding the two Eids and witr: one intends the prayer of Eid and witr without specifying them as wajib; not that he is forbidden from intending wajib, but that it is not required of him due to the difference. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 222] In nafl: he intended by nafl what includes sunan, so it includes the sunnah of Fajr as well, and likewise tarawih according to the generality of mashayikh, and that is the correct view. And the precaution is specification, so he intends taking care of its quality as tarawih or sunnah of the time. And standing, etc.: he made it absolute, but it is restricted to one who is able to do it and to ruku' and sujud, and standing does not cause him to miss a condition like purification, for example, or the ability to recite. If standing is difficult for him or he is able to stand but unable to prostrate, it is not required of him, but he is given a choice in the second rak'ah between gesturing while standing or sitting, just as if he has a wound that oozes when he prostrates, he is given a choice similarly. And if he is such that if he stands his urine drips, or if he stands he exposes his awrah which prevents prayer, or he is unable to recite while standing and while sitting none of that occurs, then sitting is obligatory. Likewise, if he is such that if he prays sitting he is able to complete and if standing he cannot. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 224] And the definition of standing is that when he extends his hands he does not reach his knees. [Maraqi al-Falah: 224] And even one verse: meaning even if he recites a short verse composed of two words like the saying of the Exalted: 'ثُمَّ نَظَرَ' [al-Muddaththir: 21] according to the apparent narration. As for the verse that is one word like 'مُدْهَامَّتَانِ' (al-Rahman: 64) or a letter like [؟], or two letters, the mashayikh differed, and the most correct view is that prayer is not valid with it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 225, 226]
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah lists the various conditions (shurut) for the opening takbir (tahrima) that initiates the prayer. The conditions are numerous and each has detailed rulings. First, there must be no gap (bila fasil) between the intention (niyyah) and the takbir; any act that breaks the continuity like eating, drinking, or speech invalidates the connection, but walking or making wudu' does not. The intention can be concurrent with the takbir (haqiqatan) or placed earlier (hukman) if no act of turning away occurs in between. Second, the takbir must be performed while standing (qa'iman) if one is able; the text clarifies that for a voluntary prayer sitting is allowed, and for one with an excuse, standing is considered fulfilled if one bends less than the ruku' position. An important issue: if one catches the imam in ruku' and bends his back, if his hands do not reach his knees, his takbir is valid as the opening takbir, but if his hands reach his knees, it is not valid. Third, the takbir must be pronounced audibly so that one can hear oneself, unless one is deaf or there is noise, in which case the condition is the ability to hear if the obstacle were removed. The mute is not required to move his tongue. Fourth, the follower (muqtadi) must intend to follow the imam. This condition includes Friday prayer, but some authorities allow one to intend Friday prayer without specifying following the imam. If one intends to follow a specific person but is mistaken, the ruling depends on the intention. Fifth, the worshipper must specify which obligatory prayer (fard) he is entering, because different obligatory prayers have different rules. For voluntary prayers (nafl) and sunan, absolute intention suffices, though it is precautionary to specify. Sixth, if the prayer is wajib (like witr, Eid, or a made-up nafl), one must specify that it is wajib, but for Eid and witr some scholars do not require mentioning 'wajib' due to differences of opinion. Seventh, the tahrima must be in Arabic if one can pronounce it; this is the correct view. Eighth, one must not lengthen the hamza of 'Allah' or the ba' of 'Akbar'. Ninth, one must say a complete sentence. Tenth, the takbir must be purely for Allah, not mixed with other words like basmala. Eleventh, one must not omit the ha' of the word 'Allah'. Twelfth, one must not add anything to the takbir that spoils it, such as adding a description of Allah that is like speech of people. The passage then discusses the conditions for standing (qiyam) in non-nafl prayers: standing is obligatory if one can do it along with ruku' and sujud, but if unable to stand or stand cannot prostrate, one may sit; in some cases sitting becomes obligatory. The definition of standing is that when one extends the arms, the hands do not reach the knees. Finally, the text covers the condition of recitation (qira'ah): at least one verse of two words is required in the first two rak'ahs of fard and in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr. A verse consisting of one word or a single letter is not sufficient according to the most correct view.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrima): The opening takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar') that initiates the prayer; its validity is governed by specific conditions.
نية المتابعة (niyyat al-mutaba'ah): The intention of the follower (muqtadi) to follow the imam in prayer; a condition for the validity of praying behind an imam.
قائما (qa'iman): Standing upright; a condition for the opening takbir for those able, with legal consideration for those with excuses.
تعيين الفرض (ta'yin al-fard): Specifying which obligatory prayer one is entering (e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr) in the intention; required for the validity of the takbir in obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a muqtadi says the opening takbir while walking to join the row, intending to follow the imam but without specifying the prayer?
A) The tahrima is invalid because he is not standing still.
B) The tahrima is valid because the intention of following suffices and walking does not break the connection.
C) The tahrima is valid only if he specified the prayer as Zuhr.
D) The tahrima is invalid because he must be standing upright and not moving.

Key Takeaway
The validity of the opening takbir depends on a combination of conditions including intention concurrence, standing, audible pronunciation, following intention (for muqtadi), specification of the prayer type, and correct Arabic wording.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for the Follower in Prayer
Expands conditions for the follower with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the follower in prayer and explain the rulings on intention, specification, standing, and recitation behind the imam.

Core Idea
The follower must intend to follow, specify the prayer, stand if able, and listen—never recite behind the imam.

This lesson details the conditions that apply specifically to a person praying behind an imam (muqtadi). These conditions go beyond the general prerequisites of prayer, addressing intention to follow, specifying the obligatory or necessary prayer, standing, and the crucial rule of listening in silence. Understanding these conditions ensures the follower's prayer is valid and complete according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main conditions
Begin by listing the key conditions mentioned for the follower: intention (niyyah), specification (ta'yin) of the obligatory (fard) or necessary (wajib) prayer, standing (qiyam), and recitation (qira'ah—but note that the follower does not recite; the imam recites).
The passage also discusses the condition of specifying the imam, but that is not a strict condition.
2
Distinguish between specification for fard, wajib, and nafl
Understand when specification is required: for fard and wajib prayers, the follower must specify which one (e.g., Zuhr, Witr). For nafl (including sunnah), specification is not required, though caution recommends it.
Wajib includes make-up of spoiled nafl, vows, witr, tawaf, and Eid prayers, but for Eid and witr one does not have to specify 'wajib'.
3
Analyze the ruling on the follower's recitation
The follower must not recite behind the imam; he listens and remains silent. Recitation is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). This is a key difference from the Shafi'i school, which requires al-Fatiha of the follower.
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad held that in silent prayers the follower may recite, but the mufta bihi is absolute prohibition.
4
Examine the condition of standing
Standing is required only if the follower can stand, bow, and prostrate without difficulty. If standing causes harm (e.g., urine dripping, exposure of awrah, inability to recite), then sitting becomes obligatory.
The definition of standing: the hands when extended do not reach the knees.
5
Determine the minimum recitation for the imam
The imam's recitation must include at least one verse of two words (e.g., 'thumma nazara'). Verses that are single words or letters (like 'مُدْهَامَّتَانِ' or 'حم') are not sufficient according to the relied-upon opinion.
This affects the follower because the follower's prayer depends on the imam's valid recitation.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة

شروط الصلاة وأركانها

للمقتدي، وتعيين الفرض، وتعيين الواجب ولا يشترط التعيين في النفل، والقيام في غير النفل، والقراءة ولو آية في ركعتي الفرض وكل النفل والوتر، ولم يتعين شيء فلا يلزم في النفل وصلية من القرآن لصحة الصلاة، ولا يقرأ المؤتم بل يستمع وينصت، وإن قرأ كره تحريما،

للمقتدي: أطلق في اشتراط نية المتابعة فشمل الجمعة، لكن في "الذخيرة" و "فتاوى قاضي خان": لو نوى الجمعة و لم ينو الاقتداء بالإمام فإنه يجوز؛ لأن الجمعة لا تكون إلا مع الإمام، وأفاد أن تعيين الإمام ليس بشرط في صحة الاقتداء، فلو نوى الاقتداء بالإمام وهو يظن أنه زيد فإذا هو عمرو يصح، إلا إذا نوى الاقتداء بزيد فإذا هو عمرو فإنه لا يصح؛ لأن العبرة لما نوى، وقيد بـ"المقتدي"؛ لأن الإمام يشترط في صحة اقتداء الرجال به نية الإمامة؛ لأنه منفرد في حق نفسه، ألا ترى أنه لو حلف أن لا يؤم أحداً، فصلى ونوى أن لا يؤم أحداً فصلى خلفه جماعة لم يحنث؛ لأن شرط الحنث أن يقصد الإمامة و لم يوجد. [البحر الرائق: ٥٥٠/١] وتعيين الفرض: أي السادس من شروط التحريمة تعيين الفرض في ابتداء الشروع، حتى لو نوى فرضاً وشرع فيه، ثم نسي فظنه تطوعاً فأتمه على ظنه، فهو فرض مسقط، وكذا عكسه يكون تطوعاً. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٢] وتعيين الواجب : أطلقه فشمل قضاء نفل أفسده والنذر والوتر وركعتي الطواف والعيدين لاختلاف الأسباب، وقالوا في العيدين والوتر: ينوي صلاة العيد والوتر من غير تقييد بالواجب، ليس المراد أنه ممنوع عن نية الواجب، بل أنه لا يلزمه ذلك للاختلاف مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٢٢] في النفل: أراد بالنفل ما يعم السنن، فشمل سنة الفجر أيضًا، وكذا التراويح عند عامة المشايخ، وهو الصحيح، والاحتياط التعيين، فينوي مراعياً صفتها بالتراويح أو سنة الوقت.

والقيام إلخ: أطلقه وهو مقيد بمن إذا قدر عليه وعلى الركوع والسجود ولا يفوته بقيامه شرط طهارة مثلاً، ولا قدرة القراءة، فلو تعسّر عليه القيام أو قدر عليه وعجز عن السجود لا يلزمه، لكنه يخير في الثانية بين الإيماء قائماً أو قاعداً كما لو كان معه جرح يسيل إذا سجد، فإنه يخير كذلك، ولو كان بحيث لو قام سلس بوله، أو لو قام ينكشف من العورة ما يمنع الصلاة، أو يعجز عن القراءة حال القيام وفي القعود لا يحصل شيء من ذلك يجب القعود، وكذا إن كان بحيث لو صلى قاعداً قدر على الإتمام وقائماً .لا. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٢٤] وحد القيام أن يكون بحيث إذا مد يديه لا ينال ركبتيه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٤] ولو آية: أي ولو قرأ آية قصيرةً مركبةً من كلمتين كقوله تعالى: ثُمَّ نَظَرَ [المدثر : ٢١] في ظاهر الرواية، وأما الآية التي هي كلمة كــمُدْهَامَّتَانِ (الرحمن: ٦٤) أو حرف كـ خاص ، فون ، ورق أو حرفان فقد اختلف المشايخ، والأصح أنه لا تجوز ك حم ، وطس أو حروف كـ حم عسق بها الصلاة. [ مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٥، ٢٢٦]
Book of Prayer. Conditions of prayer and its pillars. For the follower: specifying the obligatory [act], specifying the necessary [act], and specifying is not required in supererogatory [prayers]. Standing in other than supererogatory, and recitation, even one verse, in the two rak'ahs of the obligatory and all supererogatory and witr. Nothing is specified, so nothing is required in supererogatory. A connection from the Quran for the validity of prayer. The follower does not recite but listens and remains silent. If he recites, it is prohibitively disliked. For the follower: [The text] was absolute in requiring the intention of following, thus it includes Friday. But in al-Dhakhirah and Fatawa Qadi Khan: If one intends Friday but does not intend to follow the imam, it is permissible, because Friday is only with the imam. [It] indicates that specifying the imam is not a condition for the validity of following. So if one intends to follow the imam thinking he is Zayd, but it is 'Amr, it is valid, unless he intended to follow Zayd but it is 'Amr, then it is not valid, because consideration is given to what he intended. [The text] qualified with 'follower' because for the imam, intention of leading is required for the validity of men following him, since he is alone regarding himself. Do you not see that if he swore not to lead anyone, then prayed intending not to lead anyone, and a congregation prayed behind him, he does not break his oath, because the condition for breaking is intending leadership, which is absent. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/550] Specifying the obligatory: i.e., the sixth condition of the initiating takbir: specifying the obligatory at the beginning of commencement, such that if one intended an obligatory [prayer] and started it, then forgot and thought it was supererogatory and completed it based on that thought, it is an obligatory [prayer] that fulfills [the obligation]; and similarly the opposite becomes supererogatory. [Maraqi al-Falah 222] Specifying the necessary: [The text] gave it absolutely, so it includes making up a spoiled supererogatory, vows, witr, the two rak'ahs of circumambulation, and the two 'Eids, due to differing causes. They said regarding 'Eid and witr: one intends the 'Eid prayer and witr without specifying 'necessary'; it is not meant that one is prohibited from intending 'necessary', rather that it is not required due to the difference. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 222] Regarding supererogatory: By supererogatory, [the author] meant what includes sunnahs, so it includes the sunnah of Fajr as well, and also tarawih according to most scholars, and that is correct. Precaution is specification, so one intends taking into account its quality as tarawih or sunnah of the time. Standing etc.: [The text] gave it absolutely, but it is qualified for one who has ability for it and for bowing and prostration, and by standing he does not miss a condition like purity, and has ability for recitation. So if standing is difficult for him, or he has ability but is unable to prostrate, it is not required; but he is given a choice in the second between gesturing while standing or sitting, as in the case of a wound that flows if he prostrates, similarly he is given choice. If it is such that if he stands his urine drips, or if he stands his private part becomes exposed preventing prayer, or he is unable to recite while standing but in sitting none of that occurs, then sitting is obligatory. Similarly, if it is such that if he prays sitting he can complete it but if standing he cannot. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 224] The definition of standing: it is such that if he extends his hands they do not reach his knees. [Maraqi al-Falah 224] Even one verse: i.e., even if he recites a short verse composed of two words, like His statement 'Then he looked' [74:21] in the apparent narration. As for a verse that is a single word like 'dark green' [55:64] or a letter like 'ص' 'ق' 'ن' or two letters, the scholars have differed, and the most correct is that prayer is not valid with [such as] 'حم', 'طس', or letters like 'حم عسق'. [Maraqi al-Falah 225-226]
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the conditions of prayer for the follower (muqtadi). It clarifies that the follower must form the intention to follow the imam, specify whether the prayer is obligatory (fard) or necessary (wajib), and that in supererogatory (nafl) prayers, specification is not required. The follower must not recite behind the imam; he should listen attentively and remain silent. Recitation by the follower is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi). The commentary then discusses nuances: the follower's intention to follow is absolute, but specific circumstances affect validity (e.g., if he intends Friday prayer but does not intend to follow the imam, it is still valid because Friday can only be with an imam). Specifying the imam is not a condition; if the follower intends to follow the imam thinking he is Zayd but it is 'Amr, it is valid, unless he specifically intended Zayd. Intention of leading is required for the imam. Then it explains that 'specifying the fard' means declaring which obligatory prayer at the start; if one forgets and mistakes it for nafl, it counts as the fard anyway, and vice versa. For wajib, it includes makeup of spoiled nafl, vows, witr, tawaf rak'ahs, and Eid prayers, but for Eid and witr one does not need to specify 'wajib' due to differing causes. In nafl, caution is to specify. The passage then details the condition of standing: it is only required for those able to stand, bow, and prostrate without harm. If standing causes difficulty or inability to prostrate, it is not required, and one may gesture. If standing causes urine dripping or exposure of awrah or inability to recite, then sitting is obligatory. The definition of standing is given. Finally, the minimum recitation: a verse of at least two words like 'thumma nazara' is sufficient. Single-word verses or letters are insufficient according to the relied-upon opinion. Throughout, the commentary follows the author's order, providing rulings with conditions and exceptions.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.
تعيين الفرض (ta'yin al-fard): Specifying the particular obligatory prayer being performed (e.g., Zuhr, Asr).
تعيين الواجب (ta'yin al-wajib): Specifying a necessary prayer that is not fard (e.g., witr, Eid).
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayers, including sunnah and nafl proper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the follower reciting behind the imam in a loud prayer?
A) It is Sunnah
B) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
C) It is wajib
D) It is permissible without dislike

Key Takeaway
The follower must not recite behind the imam; he listens and remains silent, and recitation is prohibitively disliked.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Conditions of the Place of Prostration
Conditions for prostration place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid place of prostration and identify when prostration is invalid or disliked.

Core Idea
Prostration requires a firm, dry surface no higher than half a cubit above the feet; exceptions exist for crowding.

This lesson focuses on the physical requirements for where a person prostrates during prayer. We will examine the conditions of firmness, permissible elevation, and exceptions such as prostrating on one's palm or garment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the requirement of firmness and dryness
The surface must be firm so the forehead does not sink, and it must be dry. Prostration on cotton, snow, or straw is invalid unless firmness is achieved.
Firmness means the head does not sink further when pressed.
2
Note the maximum elevation difference
The place of prostration should not be more than half a cubit higher than the feet. Slight elevation less than half a cubit is permissible.
Half a cubit is roughly the length from elbow to fingertips.
3
Recognize the exceptions: prostrating on palm or garment
It is valid to prostrate on one's palm or the edge of one's garment if it is dry, but it is disliked without an excuse.
The palm must be that of the person prostrating.
4
Understand the ruling on non-firm substances
Prostration on cotton, snow, or hay is invalid unless the surface is firm enough to prevent sinking.
If the substance is compacted and firm, it may become valid.

كتاب الصلاة

شروط الصلاة وأركانها

والركوع والسجود على ما يجد حجمه وتستقر عليه جبهته ولو على كفه أو طرف أي الساجد يبسه

وصلية

ثوبه إن طهر محل وضعه وسجد وجوبا بما صلب أنفه من وبجبهته، ولا يصح

الكف أو الطرف

الاقتصار على الأنف إلا من عذر بالجبهة وعدم ارتفاع محل السجود عن موضع

القدمين بأكثر من نصف ذراع، وإن زاد على نصف ذراع لم يجز السجود إلا لزحمة

والارتفاع القليل لا يضر

سجد فيها على ظهر مصل صلاته، ووضع اليدين والركبتين في الصحيح، ووضع شيء من أصابع الرجلين حالة السجود على الأرض، ولا يكفي وضع ظاهر القدم،

وتقديم الركوع على السجود، والرفع من السجود إلى قرب القعود.

والركوع وهو الانحناء بالظهر والرأس جميعاً، وكماله بتسوية الرأس بالعجز. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٨] والسجود: السجدة إنما تتحقق بوضع الجبهة لا الأنف وحده مع وضع إحدى اليدين وإحدى الركبتين وشيء من أطراف أصابع إحدى القدمين على طاهر من الأرض، وإلا فلا وجود لها، ومع ذلك البعض تصح على المختار مع الكراهة، وتمام السجود بإتيانه بالواجب فيه، ويتحقق بوضع جميع اليدين والركبتين والقدمين والجيهة والأنف. مراقي الفلاح: ۲۲۹، ۲۳۱] على ما يجد إلخ أي بحيث لو بالغ لا يتسفل رأسه أبلغ مما كان حال الوضع، فلا يصح

السجود على القطن والثلج والتبن والأرز والذرة إلا إذا وجد اليبس مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣١] ولو على كفه: أي ويصح السجود لو كان على كفه أي الساجد في الصحيح أو كان السجود على طرف ثوبه أي الساجد، ويكره بغير عذر مراقي الفلاح: ۲۳۱] على ظهر مصل: قيد بقيدين: أحدهما: أن يكون المسجود عليه مصلياً، والآخر اتحاد صلاة الساجد والمسجود عليه، فإن انتفى كلاهما أو أحدهما بأن لم يكن ذلك المسجود عليه مصلياً أو كان في صلاة أخرى لا يصح السجود ووضع وضع إحدى اليدين، وإحدى الركبتين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٢]

وتقديم الركوع إلخ: أي ويشترط لصحة الركوع والسجود تقديم الركوع على السجود. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٢] ومقتضاه أنه إذا ركع قبل أن يقرأ أو سجد قبل أن يركع فسدت، وفي "الكافي" ما يفيده، وفيه من سجود السهو: لو قدم ركنا عن ركن سجد للسهو، وهذا يقتضي وجوب رعاية الترتيب دون فرضيته، وفيه تناقض، وأجاب صاحب جامع الفصولين" العلامة ابن قاضي سماوة في شرح التسهيل" بأن معنى فرضية الترتيب توقف صحة الثاني على وجود الأول، حتى لوركع بعد السجود لا يكون السجود معتدا به، فيلزمه إعادته، ومعنى وجوبه: أن الإخلال به لا يفسد الصلاة إذا أعاده حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣٣]
Book of Prayer. Conditions of prayer and its pillars. And bowing and prostration: on a surface that has firmness and on which his forehead settles, even if on his palm or the edge of his garment if it is dry. [He] prostrates obligatorily with his forehead and the hard part of his nose. It is not valid to limit to the nose except due to an excuse of the forehead. And the place of prostration should not be higher than the place of the feet by more than half a cubit; if it exceeds half a cubit, prostration is not permitted except due to crowding; slight elevation does not harm. [If] he prostrated on the back of a person in prayer whose prayer is the same as his, and placing the hands and knees [is required] according to the sound view, and placing some of the toes during prostration on the ground; placing the top of the foot is not sufficient. And precedence of bowing over prostration, and rising from prostration to near sitting. Bowing: it is bending the back and head together; its perfection is leveling the head with the back. [Maraqi al-Falah 228] Prostration: the prostration is only realized by placing the forehead, not just the nose, along with placing one hand, one knee, and some of the tips of the toes of one foot on a pure part of the ground; otherwise it does not exist. However, some [scholars] say it is valid according to the chosen view with dislike. The complete prostration is performing its obligatory parts, and is realized by placing all hands, knees, feet, forehead, and nose. [Maraqi al-Falah 229, 231] 'On a surface that has firmness' etc. means such that if he presses hard, his head does not sink more than it was when placed. So prostration on cotton, snow, straw, rice, or corn is not valid unless firmness is found. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 231] 'Even on his palm': it is valid to prostrate on his own palm according to the sound view, or on the edge of his garment, but it is disliked without excuse. [Maraqi al-Falah 231] 'On the back of a person in prayer': qualified by two conditions: first, that the one prostrated on is in prayer, and second, that the prayer of the one prostrating and the one prostrated on is the same. If both or one of them is absent—i.e., the one prostrated on is not in prayer or is in a different prayer—prostration is not valid. And placing one hand and one knee [is sufficient]. [Maraqi al-Falah 232] 'Precedence of bowing' etc.: it is required for the validity of bowing and prostration that bowing precedes prostration. [Maraqi al-Falah 232] Its import is that if he bows before reciting or prostrates before bowing, the prayer is invalid. In al-Kafi there is something supporting this. And in it regarding prostrations of forgetfulness: if one advances a pillar over another, he performs prostrations of forgetfulness. This necessitates that observing the order is obligatory (wajib) not obligatory integral (fard). There is an apparent contradiction. The author of Jami' al-Fusulayn, 'Allamah Ibn Qadi Samawah, in Sharh al-Tashil, answered that the meaning of the obligation of order (fardiyyah) is that the validity of the second depends on the existence of the first, such that if he bows after prostration, the prostration is not considered, so he must repeat it. And the meaning of its obligation (wujub) is that violating it does not invalidate the prayer if he repeats [the missed act]. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 233]
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage details the conditions for bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) in prayer. It begins by stating that prostration must be on a firm, dry surface where the forehead can rest; it may be on one's palm or garment if the garment is dry and clean. The obligatory parts (wajib) of prostration are the forehead and the hard part of the nose; it is not sufficient to use only the nose unless there is an excuse concerning the forehead. The place of prostration must not be more than half a cubit higher than the feet; slight elevation is fine. Prostration on the back of a person who is in the same prayer as the prostrator is valid under two conditions: the person must be praying, and the prayers must be identical. Otherwise, it is invalid. The hands and knees must be placed; placing some toes (not just the top of the foot) is required in the sound view. The order of bowing before prostration is obligatory (wajib) but not integral (fard)—meaning if reversed, the prayer is not invalidated if the order is rectified, but the act must be repeated. Bowing is defined as bending the back and head together, ideally leveling the head with the back. Complete prostration involves the forehead, nose, both hands, both knees, and toes. The commentary resolves a potential contradiction between the validity of reversing order and the need for prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) by explaining that order is obligatory but not fard; violating it requires repetition but does not invalidate the entire prayer.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration: placing the forehead, nose, hands, knees, and toes on the ground in a specific manner.
الركوع (al-ruku'): Bowing: bending the back and head until the head is level with the back.
فرضية الترتيب (fardiyyat al-tartib): The integral nature of the order between ruku' and sujud—if integral, violating it invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum permissible elevation of the prostration place relative to the feet?
A) One cubit
B) Half a cubit
C) No limit
D) One handspan

Key Takeaway
A valid prostration requires a firm, dry place not higher than half a cubit above the feet; slight elevation is permissible, and prostrating on non-firm substances is invalid unless firm.

Obligatory Parts of Prostration (Wajibat al-Sujud)
Wajibat of sujud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the wajib parts of prostration and distinguish between the minimal valid form and the complete sunnah form.

Core Idea
Prostration is only realized by placing the forehead and at least one hand, one knee, and some toes; the complete form includes all body parts.

This lesson focuses on what must be placed on the ground during sujud. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the wajib (obligatory) elements that must be present for the act to count, and the sunnah elements that complete it. We will also learn the ruling for using only the nose.

Guided Path
1
Note the wajib elements of prostration
The text states that prostration is realized by placing the forehead (not just the nose) and at least one hand, one knee, and some toes. These are the minimum wajib parts.
The forehead must touch the ground; the nose is also wajib but not sufficient alone.
2
Understand the ruling for using only the nose
Placing only the nose without the forehead is not valid unless there is an excuse such as a wound on the forehead.
This is a concession for valid excuses.
3
Distinguish minimal valid from complete form
The complete prostration (tamam) includes all seven parts: forehead, nose, both hands, both knees, and toes of both feet. The minimal form uses one of each limb.
Performing the complete form is sunnah and more rewarding.
4
Recognize the consequence of missing a wajib
If a wajib part is omitted (e.g., leaving out the knee), the prostration is valid but deficient, and sajdat al-sahw may be required.
The text mentions 'its complete prostration is performing its wajibat' – fulfilling all wajibat is necessary for completeness.

شروط الصلاة وأركانها

والركوع والسجود على ما يجد حجمه وتستقر عليه جبهته ولو على كفه أو طرف أي الساجد يبسه

وصلية

ثوبه إن طهر محل وضعه وسجد وجوبا بما صلب أنفه من وبجبهته، ولا يصح

الكف أو الطرف

الاقتصار على الأنف إلا من عذر بالجبهة وعدم ارتفاع محل السجود عن موضع

القدمين بأكثر من نصف ذراع، وإن زاد على نصف ذراع لم يجز السجود إلا لزحمة

والارتفاع القليل لا يضر

سجد فيها على ظهر مصل صلاته، ووضع اليدين والركبتين في الصحيح، ووضع شيء من أصابع الرجلين حالة السجود على الأرض، ولا يكفي وضع ظاهر القدم،

وتقديم الركوع على السجود، والرفع من السجود إلى قرب القعود.

والركوع وهو الانحناء بالظهر والرأس جميعاً، وكماله بتسوية الرأس بالعجز. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٨] والسجود: السجدة إنما تتحقق بوضع الجبهة لا الأنف وحده مع وضع إحدى اليدين وإحدى الركبتين وشيء من أطراف أصابع إحدى القدمين على طاهر من الأرض، وإلا فلا وجود لها، ومع ذلك البعض تصح على المختار مع الكراهة، وتمام السجود بإتيانه بالواجب فيه، ويتحقق بوضع جميع اليدين والركبتين والقدمين والجيهة والأنف. مراقي الفلاح: ۲۲۹، ۲۳۱] على ما يجد إلخ أي بحيث لو بالغ لا يتسفل رأسه أبلغ مما كان حال الوضع، فلا يصح

السجود على القطن والثلج والتبن والأرز والذرة إلا إذا وجد اليبس مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣١] ولو على كفه: أي ويصح السجود لو كان على كفه أي الساجد في الصحيح أو كان السجود على طرف ثوبه أي الساجد، ويكره بغير عذر مراقي الفلاح: ۲۳۱] على ظهر مصل: قيد بقيدين: أحدهما: أن يكون المسجود عليه مصلياً، والآخر اتحاد صلاة الساجد والمسجود عليه، فإن انتفى كلاهما أو أحدهما بأن لم يكن ذلك المسجود عليه مصلياً أو كان في صلاة أخرى لا يصح السجود ووضع وضع إحدى اليدين، وإحدى الركبتين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٢]

وتقديم الركوع إلخ: أي ويشترط لصحة الركوع والسجود تقديم الركوع على السجود. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٢] ومقتضاه أنه إذا ركع قبل أن يقرأ أو سجد قبل أن يركع فسدت، وفي "الكافي" ما يفيده، وفيه من سجود السهو: لو قدم ركنا عن ركن سجد للسهو، وهذا يقتضي وجوب رعاية الترتيب دون فرضيته، وفيه تناقض، وأجاب صاحب جامع الفصولين" العلامة ابن قاضي سماوة في شرح التسهيل" بأن معنى فرضية الترتيب توقف صحة الثاني على وجود الأول، حتى لوركع بعد السجود لا يكون السجود معتدا به، فيلزمه إعادته، ومعنى وجوبه: أن الإخلال به لا يفسد الصلاة إذا أعاده حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣٣]
Book of Prayer. Conditions of prayer and its pillars. And bowing and prostration: on a surface that has firmness and on which his forehead settles, even if on his palm or the edge of his garment if it is dry. [He] prostrates obligatorily with his forehead and the hard part of his nose. It is not valid to limit to the nose except due to an excuse of the forehead. And the place of prostration should not be higher than the place of the feet by more than half a cubit; if it exceeds half a cubit, prostration is not permitted except due to crowding; slight elevation does not harm. [If] he prostrated on the back of a person in prayer whose prayer is the same as his, and placing the hands and knees [is required] according to the sound view, and placing some of the toes during prostration on the ground; placing the top of the foot is not sufficient. And precedence of bowing over prostration, and rising from prostration to near sitting. Bowing: it is bending the back and head together; its perfection is leveling the head with the back. [Maraqi al-Falah 228] Prostration: the prostration is only realized by placing the forehead, not just the nose, along with placing one hand, one knee, and some of the tips of the toes of one foot on a pure part of the ground; otherwise it does not exist. However, some [scholars] say it is valid according to the chosen view with dislike. The complete prostration is performing its obligatory parts, and is realized by placing all hands, knees, feet, forehead, and nose. [Maraqi al-Falah 229, 231] 'On a surface that has firmness' etc. means such that if he presses hard, his head does not sink more than it was when placed. So prostration on cotton, snow, straw, rice, or corn is not valid unless firmness is found. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 231] 'Even on his palm': it is valid to prostrate on his own palm according to the sound view, or on the edge of his garment, but it is disliked without excuse. [Maraqi al-Falah 231] 'On the back of a person in prayer': qualified by two conditions: first, that the one prostrated on is in prayer, and second, that the prayer of the one prostrating and the one prostrated on is the same. If both or one of them is absent—i.e., the one prostrated on is not in prayer or is in a different prayer—prostration is not valid. And placing one hand and one knee [is sufficient]. [Maraqi al-Falah 232] 'Precedence of bowing' etc.: it is required for the validity of bowing and prostration that bowing precedes prostration. [Maraqi al-Falah 232] Its import is that if he bows before reciting or prostrates before bowing, the prayer is invalid. In al-Kafi there is something supporting this. And in it regarding prostrations of forgetfulness: if one advances a pillar over another, he performs prostrations of forgetfulness. This necessitates that observing the order is obligatory (wajib) not obligatory integral (fard). There is an apparent contradiction. The author of Jami' al-Fusulayn, 'Allamah Ibn Qadi Samawah, in Sharh al-Tashil, answered that the meaning of the obligation of order (fardiyyah) is that the validity of the second depends on the existence of the first, such that if he bows after prostration, the prostration is not considered, so he must repeat it. And the meaning of its obligation (wujub) is that violating it does not invalidate the prayer if he repeats [the missed act]. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 233]
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage details the conditions for bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) in prayer. It begins by stating that prostration must be on a firm, dry surface where the forehead can rest; it may be on one's palm or garment if the garment is dry and clean. The obligatory parts (wajib) of prostration are the forehead and the hard part of the nose; it is not sufficient to use only the nose unless there is an excuse concerning the forehead. The place of prostration must not be more than half a cubit higher than the feet; slight elevation is fine. Prostration on the back of a person who is in the same prayer as the prostrator is valid under two conditions: the person must be praying, and the prayers must be identical. Otherwise, it is invalid. The hands and knees must be placed; placing some toes (not just the top of the foot) is required in the sound view. The order of bowing before prostration is obligatory (wajib) but not integral (fard)—meaning if reversed, the prayer is not invalidated if the order is rectified, but the act must be repeated. Bowing is defined as bending the back and head together, ideally leveling the head with the back. Complete prostration involves the forehead, nose, both hands, both knees, and toes. The commentary resolves a potential contradiction between the validity of reversing order and the need for prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) by explaining that order is obligatory but not fard; violating it requires repetition but does not invalidate the entire prayer.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration: placing the forehead, nose, hands, knees, and toes on the ground in a specific manner.
الركوع (al-ruku'): Bowing: bending the back and head until the head is level with the back.
فرضية الترتيب (fardiyyat al-tartib): The integral nature of the order between ruku' and sujud—if integral, violating it invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a wajib part of prostration according to the Hanafi school?
A) Forehead
B) Nose
C) Both hands
D) At least one knee

Key Takeaway
Prostration is valid only with at least the forehead, nose, one hand, one knee, and some toes; the complete form includes all seven parts but is sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Order of Ruku' and Sujud (Tartib)
Order of ruku' and sujud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that the order of ruku' before sujud is wajib not fard, and describe the practical implication of reversal.

Core Idea
Reversing ruku' and sujud does not invalidate the prayer but requires repetition of the correct order and sajdat al-sahw.

This lesson addresses a key Hanafi distinction: the order of ruku' before sujud is wajib (obligatory) but not fard (integral). This means if someone prostrates before bowing, the prayer is not nullified; they must repeat the missed bowing and perform prostration of forgetfulness. We will also examine the apparent contradiction in the texts and the resolution provided by Ibn Qadi Samawah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling that bowing must precede prostration
The text states: 'ويشترط لصحة الركوع والسجود تقديم الركوع على السجود' – it is a condition for validity that bowing precedes prostration.
This is the basic rule.
2
Understand the apparent contradiction in sources
One source (al-Kafi) says that if one prostrates before bowing, the prayer is invalid. Another source says that if one advances a rukn over another, sajdat al-sahw is performed, implying the prayer is still valid. This seems contradictory.
The contradiction concerns whether order is fard (invalidates) or wajib (requires correction).
3
Apply the resolution from Ibn Qadi Samawah
The resolution distinguishes: order is fard (fardiyyah) in the sense that the second act depends on the first – if you bow after prostration, the prostration is not considered; you must repeat it. But order is wajib (wujub) in that violating it does not invalidate the whole prayer if you correct it.
This resolves the contradiction: the prayer is not invalidated, but the missed act must be repeated.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school considers order to be a rukn; violating it invalidates the prayer. The Hanafi school's nuance aims to preserve the prayer's validity while requiring correction.
This is a thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

كتاب الصلاة

شروط الصلاة وأركانها

والركوع والسجود على ما يجد حجمه وتستقر عليه جبهته ولو على كفه أو طرف أي الساجد يبسه

وصلية

ثوبه إن طهر محل وضعه وسجد وجوبا بما صلب أنفه من وبجبهته، ولا يصح

الكف أو الطرف

الاقتصار على الأنف إلا من عذر بالجبهة وعدم ارتفاع محل السجود عن موضع

القدمين بأكثر من نصف ذراع، وإن زاد على نصف ذراع لم يجز السجود إلا لزحمة

والارتفاع القليل لا يضر

سجد فيها على ظهر مصل صلاته، ووضع اليدين والركبتين في الصحيح، ووضع شيء من أصابع الرجلين حالة السجود على الأرض، ولا يكفي وضع ظاهر القدم،

وتقديم الركوع على السجود، والرفع من السجود إلى قرب القعود.

والركوع وهو الانحناء بالظهر والرأس جميعاً، وكماله بتسوية الرأس بالعجز. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٨] والسجود: السجدة إنما تتحقق بوضع الجبهة لا الأنف وحده مع وضع إحدى اليدين وإحدى الركبتين وشيء من أطراف أصابع إحدى القدمين على طاهر من الأرض، وإلا فلا وجود لها، ومع ذلك البعض تصح على المختار مع الكراهة، وتمام السجود بإتيانه بالواجب فيه، ويتحقق بوضع جميع اليدين والركبتين والقدمين والجيهة والأنف. مراقي الفلاح: ۲۲۹، ۲۳۱] على ما يجد إلخ أي بحيث لو بالغ لا يتسفل رأسه أبلغ مما كان حال الوضع، فلا يصح

السجود على القطن والثلج والتبن والأرز والذرة إلا إذا وجد اليبس مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣١] ولو على كفه: أي ويصح السجود لو كان على كفه أي الساجد في الصحيح أو كان السجود على طرف ثوبه أي الساجد، ويكره بغير عذر مراقي الفلاح: ۲۳۱] على ظهر مصل: قيد بقيدين: أحدهما: أن يكون المسجود عليه مصلياً، والآخر اتحاد صلاة الساجد والمسجود عليه، فإن انتفى كلاهما أو أحدهما بأن لم يكن ذلك المسجود عليه مصلياً أو كان في صلاة أخرى لا يصح السجود ووضع وضع إحدى اليدين، وإحدى الركبتين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٢]

وتقديم الركوع إلخ: أي ويشترط لصحة الركوع والسجود تقديم الركوع على السجود. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٢] ومقتضاه أنه إذا ركع قبل أن يقرأ أو سجد قبل أن يركع فسدت، وفي "الكافي" ما يفيده، وفيه من سجود السهو: لو قدم ركنا عن ركن سجد للسهو، وهذا يقتضي وجوب رعاية الترتيب دون فرضيته، وفيه تناقض، وأجاب صاحب جامع الفصولين" العلامة ابن قاضي سماوة في شرح التسهيل" بأن معنى فرضية الترتيب توقف صحة الثاني على وجود الأول، حتى لوركع بعد السجود لا يكون السجود معتدا به، فيلزمه إعادته، ومعنى وجوبه: أن الإخلال به لا يفسد الصلاة إذا أعاده حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣٣]

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Prostration on a Person in Prayer (Sujud 'ala Dhahr Musalli)
Special case of prostration on a person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid prostration on a person's back and identify when it is invalid.

Core Idea
Prostrating on a praying person's back is valid only if both are in the same prayer and the person is actually praying.

This lesson covers a specific case from the text: prostrating on the back of another person during prayer. This can occur in very crowded congregational prayers. The Hanafi school sets two conditions for it to be valid: the person being prostrated on must be in prayer, and that prayer must be the same as the prostrator's. We will also note that the minimal placement of hands and knees is sufficient in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Note the two conditions for valid prostration on a person
The text states two conditions: 1) the person being prostrated on must be in prayer (musalli), and 2) his prayer must be the same as the prostrator's prayer (same intention and type).
If either condition is missing, the prostration is invalid.
2
Understand the implication of missing conditions
If the person is not praying, or is in a different prayer (e.g., fard vs sunnah), prostration on his back is invalid.
The prostration would not count, and the prayer of the prostrator is affected.
3
Recognize that minimal limb placement suffices
The text concludes that placing one hand and one knee is sufficient when prostrating on a person's back, unlike the usual requirement of both hands and knees? Actually it says 'وضع إحدى اليدين و إحدى الركبتين' meaning only one hand and one knee need to be placed in this situation.
This is a concession due to the difficulty of placing all limbs on a person's back.

However, some [scholars] say it is valid according to the chosen view with dislike. The complete prostration is performing its obligatory parts, and is realized by placing all hands, knees, feet, forehead, and nose. [Maraqi al-Falah 229, 231] 'On a surface that has firmness' etc. means such that if he presses hard, his head does not sink more than it was when placed. So prostration on cotton, snow, straw, rice, or corn is not valid unless firmness is found. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 231] 'Even on his palm': it is valid to prostrate on his own palm according to the sound view, or on the edge of his garment, but it is disliked without excuse. [Maraqi al-Falah 231] 'On the back of a person in prayer': qualified by two conditions: first, that the one prostrated on is in prayer, and second, that the prayer of the one prostrating and the one prostrated on is the same. If both or one of them is absent—i.e., the one prostrated on is not in prayer or is in a different prayer—prostration is not valid. And placing one hand and one knee [is sufficient]. [Maraqi al-Falah 232] 'Precedence of bowing' etc.: it is required for the validity of bowing and prostration that bowing precedes prostration. [Maraqi al-Falah 232] Its import is that if he bows before reciting or prostrates before bowing, the prayer is invalid. In al-Kafi there is something supporting this. And in it regarding prostrations of forgetfulness: if one advances a pillar over another, he performs prostrations of forgetfulness. This necessitates that observing the order is obligatory (wajib) not obligatory integral (fard). There is an apparent contradiction. The author of Jami' al-Fusulayn, 'Allamah Ibn Qadi Samawah, in Sharh al-Tashil, answered that the meaning of the obligation of order (fardiyyah) is that the validity of the second depends on the existence of the first, such that if he bows after prostration, the prostration is not considered, so he must repeat it. And the meaning of its obligation (wujub) is that violating it does not invalidate the prayer if he repeats [the missed act]. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 233]
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage details the conditions for bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) in prayer. It begins by stating that prostration must be on a firm, dry surface where the forehead can rest; it may be on one's palm or garment if the garment is dry and clean. The obligatory parts (wajib) of prostration are the forehead and the hard part of the nose; it is not sufficient to use only the nose unless there is an excuse concerning the forehead. The place of prostration must not be more than half a cubit higher than the feet; slight elevation is fine. Prostration on the back of a person who is in the same prayer as the prostrator is valid under two conditions: the person must be praying, and the prayers must be identical. Otherwise, it is invalid. The hands and knees must be placed; placing some toes (not just the top of the foot) is required in the sound view. The order of bowing before prostration is obligatory (wajib) but not integral (fard)—meaning if reversed, the prayer is not invalidated if the order is rectified, but the act must be repeated. Bowing is defined as bending the back and head together, ideally leveling the head with the back. Complete prostration involves the forehead, nose, both hands, both knees, and toes. The commentary resolves a potential contradiction between the validity of reversing order and the need for prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) by explaining that order is obligatory but not fard; violating it requires repetition but does not invalidate the entire prayer.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration: placing the forehead, nose, hands, knees, and toes on the ground in a specific manner.
الركوع (al-ruku'): Bowing: bending the back and head until the head is level with the back.
فرضية الترتيب (fardiyyat al-tartib): The integral nature of the order between ruku' and sujud—if integral, violating it invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is prostration on a person's back valid?
A) When the person is any Muslim
B) When the person is in the same prayer as the prostrator
C) When the person is praying any prayer
D) When there is no space on the ground

Key Takeaway
Prostration on a person's back is valid only if the person is praying the same prayer as the prostrator; if not, the prostration is invalid.
